[page 27]{.stl_10}

[58. ]{.stl_12}[Lastly, moral rights are recognized in Canada for works
such as computer programs and,  generally, for all other works in which
copyright subsists. Moral rights may not be  assigned and will therefore
continue to reside with the author of a work unless they are  waived in
whole or in part. Under Canadian law, an assignment of copyright in a
work  does not by that act alone constitute a waiver of moral rights. As
such, unless such rights  are waived, an author of video game content
may remain capable of asserting their moral  rights in a video game
product, even where all other copyrights in such content have
been  assigned.]{.stl_10}

[TRANSFER OF RIGHTS AND COMPENSATION]{.stl_10}

[59. ]{.stl_12}[Under the Canadian ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[, there are rules pertaining to first
ownership of  copyright which apply in defined instances. For example,
as described above, where the  author of a work was in the employment of
another person under a contract of service or  apprenticeship and the
work was done in the course of their employment by that person,  the
employer shall be the first owner of copyright, in the absence of any
agreement  to the  contrary.]{.stl_10}

[Apart from the foregoing situation of employment, in Canada the author
of a work is deemed to be the first owner of copyright therein pursuant
to the Canadian ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[. ]{.stl_10}[Also, in respect of a
performer's performances and sound recordings, the Canadian
]{.stl_15}[Copyright Act ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[respectively deems the performer and the
maker thereof to be the first owners of copyright in such subject
matter. In all other instances, ownership of copyright in video games
must be acquired by express contractual transfer.]{.stl_10}

[60. ]{.stl_12}[The transfer of these rights implies, for employees, a
compensation that typically has the  form of a salary in Canada. For
independent contractors, the typical compensation may  be a lump sum
where copyright has been wholly assigned; however, where
copyright  has  instead been licensed by the independent contractor who
is a first owner of the copyright,  the compensation must be
proportional, either alone or in combination with a lump sum.  In any
event, the compensation that authors shall receive is not statutorily
established, but  will depend on the negotiation between the parties
implicated in a particular video game.]{.stl_10}

[61. ]{.stl_12}[Therefore, the Canadian ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act
]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[follows the basic European
princip]{.stl_10}[les of authors' ]{.stl_15}[ rights, as video game
studios cannot attain the status of authors, and moral rights are
not  assignable, although they may be waived. Video games may have a
distributive  classification in Canada, via the protection of software,
cinematographic works or musical  works. This is why some Canadian
experts have asserted that video games could be ]{.stl_10}[ protected as
―compilations‖ and as ―collective works‖]{.stl_15}[. Finally, authors
shall have, in  principle, all the rights in the created work, unless
there is an agreement between them  and a third person, such as an
employment agreement.]{.stl_10}

[CHINA]{.stl_11}

[62. ]{.stl_12}[China has made enormous efforts to improve its
legislation on the protection of intellectual  property rights. Thus,
any works of literature, art, natural sciences, social
sciences,  engineering and technology are protected through the
]{.stl_10}[Copyright Law of the People's ]{.stl_19
style="font-style:italic;"}[ Republic of China of 2010 ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[(hereinafter, the PRC ]{.stl_10}[Copyright
Law]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[), promulgated in 1990
and  amended in 2001 and 2010. ]{.stl_10}[Although China's intellectual
property law does not ]{.stl_15}[ specifically refer to video games,
protection is available for software programs  under  copyright law. In
accordance with Article 3 of the PRC ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Law]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[, copyright  protection is available for a
variety of works, including written works, computer  software,]{.stl_10}

[page 28]{.stl_10}

[photographic works, musical works and drawings. Therefore, and although
there is no specific reference to video games, these may be works that
combine all those elements.]{.stl_10}

[CLASSIFICATION OF VIDEO GAMES]{.stl_10}

[63. ]{.stl_12}[The closest reference to video games in Chinese law is
to ―online games‖]{.stl_15}[. In accordance  with the ]{.stl_10}[Interim
Measures on Administration of Online Games ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[(the ―]{.stl_15}[Measures]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[‖) enacted in  March 2010 by the Ministry of
Culture, ―online games‖ refer to ]{.stl_15}[game products and  services
consisting of software programs and information data which are provided
via  information networks such as the Internet and mobile communication
networks.]{.stl_10}^[52\ ]{.stl_16}^[ Therefore, online games are
classified as ―computer software‖ or ―software‖.]{.stl_15}

[Furthermore, under the ]{.stl_10}[Regulations for Computer Software
Protection of 2002 ]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[(hereinafter,
the ―]{.stl_15}[RCSP]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[‖), ―computer
software‖ is defined broadly to include all types of ]{.stl_15}[computer
programs and related documentation.]{.stl_10}^[53\ ]{.stl_16}^[Within
that definition, ―computer ]{.stl_15}[prog]{.stl_10}[rams‖ means a
sequence of code]{.stl_15}[-based instructions that can be run by
devices having information processing capacity, such as computers, for
achieving a certain result, or a sequence of symbol-based instructions
or expressions that can be automatically converted into a sequence of
code-based instructions. ]{.stl_10}[―Related documentation‖ means
]{.stl_15}[all relevant written materials and diagrams, such as the
program design specifications, flow charts and operating manual that are
used to describe the contents, elements, design, functions and
specifications, development, testing results and operating method of the
program.]{.stl_10}^[54]{.stl_16}^

[64. ]{.stl_12}[Therefore, video games are not only granted protection
under the ]{.stl_10}[RCSP ]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[but
also, as with  all other software programs, may be classified as
copyrighted works under the  PRC ]{.stl_10}[ Copyright Law]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[.]{.stl_10}

[RIGHTS HOLDERS AND TRANSFER OF RIGHTS]{.stl_10}

[65. ]{.stl_12}[Viewing video games as software means a ―software
developer‖ (roughly equivalent to the ]{.stl_15}[ concept of
]{.stl_10}[author]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[, referring to
those individuals or entities that develop or organize the  software
development)]{.stl_10}^[55\ ]{.stl_16}^[owns the copyright in the
resulting video game.]{.stl_10}^[56\ ]{.stl_16}^[Video games  are often
complex technical creations completed by a group of people with
different roles,  which may involve many individuals in the value chain
such as content providers,  programmers, designers, scriptwriters, music
composers and artists. In this case, the  collective efforts of the
development team mean that these contributors are
considered  co-developers. Each co-developer enjoys the copyright in the
work it creates, and  co-developers shall jointly own the copyright, as
per Article 10 of the ]{.stl_10}[RCSP]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[.]{.stl_10}^[57]{.stl_16}^

[66. ]{.stl_12}[Publishers, who are usually also the developers in the
video game industry, play a key  role in organizing video game
development as well as placing the video game onto a  storage medium for
distribution. In contrast to traditional publishers of a book or a
CD,  video game publishers are responsible not only for publishing a
video game, but also for  the administration and upgrading of the video
game. The importance of publishers in the  industry is shown by the fact
that, to date, all video game copyright litigation in China
]{.stl_10}[--  particularly those disputes involving China's biggest
video game publisher, Shanda -- ]{.stl_15}[has  been initiated by and
against video game publishers.]{.stl_10}

[52 ]{.stl_07}[Article 2 of the ]{.stl_09}[Interim Measures on
Administration of Online Games]{.stl_17 style="font-style:italic;"}[.
]{.stl_09}[53 ]{.stl_07}[Article 2 of the ]{.stl_09}[RCSP]{.stl_17
style="font-style:italic;"}[.]{.stl_09}

[54 ]{.stl_07}[Article 3 of the ]{.stl_09}[RCSP]{.stl_17
style="font-style:italic;"}[.]{.stl_09}

[55 ]{.stl_07}[Article 3 of the ]{.stl_09}[RCSP]{.stl_17
style="font-style:italic;"}[.]{.stl_09}

[56 ]{.stl_07}[Article 9 of the ]{.stl_09}[RCSP]{.stl_17
style="font-style:italic;"}[.]{.stl_09}

[57 ]{.stl_07}[Article 10 of the ]{.stl_09}[RCSP]{.stl_17
style="font-style:italic;"}[.]{.stl_09}

[page 29]{.stl_10}

[On the othe]{.stl_10}[r hand, ―]{.stl_15}[producer]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[‖ is not a specific legal term under Chinese
law]{.stl_15}[. It may refer to the originators of concepts and ideas,
the investor or the manufacturer of software products. Generally
speaking, without a copyright transfer agreement from the developer,
covering the creation of concepts, investment or manufacturing,
copyright will not be deemed to have been vested
automatically.]{.stl_10}

[67. ]{.stl_12}[As defined by the PRC ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Law]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[, an author of a work may be either an
individual  creator or an entity responsible for organizing the work
that publishes the work under its  name and assumes all liabilities.
Accordingly, Article 11 of the PRC ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Law ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[states  the following:]{.stl_10}

[―The author of a work is the citizen who creates the work.‖]{.stl_19
style="font-style:italic;"}

[―Where a work is created u]{.stl_19 style="font-style:italic;"}[nder
the auspices and according to the intention of a legal entity or other
organization, which bears responsibility for the work, the said legal
entity or organization shall be deemed to be ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[the author of the work.‖]{.stl_19
style="font-style:italic;"}

[―The citizen, legal entity or other or]{.stl_19
style="font-style:italic;"}[ganization whose name is mentioned in
connection with a work shall, in the absence of proof to the contrary,
be ]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[deemed to be the author of the
work.‖]{.stl_19 style="font-style:italic;"}

[Therefore, where an employer-employee relationship exists, the real
contributors to the video game do not fall within the category of
author, as these vest in any case in the employer.]{.stl_10}

[68. ]{.stl_12}[In the case of multiple creators, co-authors may exist
as long as they have participated in  the creation of the work. If a
work of joint authorship can be separated into independent  parts and
exploited separately, each co-author may be entitled to independent
copyright in  the parts that he/she created, provided that the exercise
of such copyright shall not  prejudice the copyright in the joint work
as a whole.]{.stl_10}^[58]{.stl_16}^

[69. ]{.stl_12}[Any individual developer/creator employed to create the
work, particularly where the work  is undertaken in the course of
employment and mainly using the material and technical  resources of the
employer, will be considered subordinate to the employer who
is  considered the developer. In such a case, the employer, instead of
the individual  developer/creator, will be legally considered the
author;]{.stl_10}^[59\ ]{.stl_16}^[however, the creator will
be  entitled to attribution.]{.stl_10}

[70. ]{.stl_12}[Additionally, it is possible for a player of an online
game to become a ―software developer‖ ]{.stl_15}[ under the PRC
]{.stl_10}[Copyright Law ]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[as
modifications for personal enjoyment and research  purposes would not
constitute copyright infringement and other modifications may
be  possible depending on the terms and conditions set out by individual
game operators.  However, given the complexity of video games and the
restrictions put in place by most  operators, contributions by players
would be limited.]{.stl_10}

[71. ]{.stl_12}[The copyright license and/or transfer are contractual
and must be in writing, as per  Articles 24 and 25 of the PRC
]{.stl_10}[Copyright Law]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[. A
license agreement is generally required ]{.stl_10}[ for exploitation of
another person's work, although some exceptions -- ]{.stl_15}[such as
installing,]{.stl_10}

[58 ]{.stl_07}[Article 13 of the PRC ]{.stl_09}[Copyright Law]{.stl_17

style="font-style:italic;"}[.]{.stl_09}

[page 30]{.stl_10}

[displaying, transforming or storing software for study and research
purposes  ]{.stl_10}[-- ]{.stl_15}[may]{.stl_10}

[exist.]{.stl_10}^[60\ ]{.stl_16}^[Such license agreements should
include the following information:]{.stl_10}

[―(1) the category of the right to exploit the work covered by the
license; ]{.stl_19 style="font-style:italic;"}[(2) the exclusive or

license;]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}

[(3) the territory and the term covered by the license;]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}

[(4) the rates of remuneration and the means of payment; (5) the
liabilities in the case of breach of the contract; and ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[(6) other matters which the parties consider
it necessary to agree upon.‖]{.stl_19 style="font-style:italic;"}

[However, where, instead of a license, the author decides to transfer
his or her copyrights, the following points should be included in the
transfer contract:]{.stl_10}

[―(1) the title of the work;]{.stl_19 style="font-style:italic;"}

[(2) the category of the right to be transferred and the territory
covered by the transfer;]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}

[(3) the rates of the transfer fee;]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}

[(4) the date and the means of payment of the transfer fee; (5) the
liabilities in the case of breach of the contract; and ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[(6) other matters that the parties consider
it necessary to agree upon.‖]{.stl_19 style="font-style:italic;"}

[72. ]{.stl_12}[Finally, regarding the compensation to which authors are
entitled, for employees who  create a work in the course of employment
using the material and technical resources of  the employer,
compensation may be paid by way of salary and bonus or may be
separate  from the remuneration package, as set out by agreement between
the employee and the  employer. For an independent contractor, the
compensation amount is subject to  agreement by the parties.]{.stl_10}

[Nonetheless, according to Article 28 of the PRC ]{.stl_10}[Copyright
Law]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[, the rates of remuneration for
the exploitation of a work may be agreed upon by the parties and may
also be paid in accordance with the rates fixed by the administrative
department for copyright under the State Council, in conjunction with
the other departments concerned. In the absence of an explicit agreement
in the contract, the remuneration shall be paid in accordance with the
rates fixed by the said department under the State Council, in
conjunction with the other departments concerned.]{.stl_10}

[RECENT DEVELOPMENTS]{.stl_10}

[73. ]{.stl_12}[The first copyright dispute involving online games in
China took place in 2007 between  Nexon, a video game publisher from the
Republic of Korea, and Tencent, a domestic  video game publisher, before
the Beijing No. 1 Intermediate Court. The court was  provided with
comparative studies on the background drawings and display layouts of
the  video games, as well as the names used for specific in-game items.
The court concluded  that a general concept is not copyrightable and
that the existing similarities between the  video games did not rise to
the level of copyright infringement or unfair competition.
This  landmark case indicates that courts shall examine each copyrighted
aspect of a video  game, and that a similar video game created
subsequently may be considered an  infringing work only if substantial
and overall similarities exist between the two.]{.stl_10}

[74. ]{.stl_12}[The proposed Amendment to the PRC ]{.stl_10}[Copyright
Law ]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[(released for public opinion
in]{.stl_10}

[March 2012) confirms that all authors of a video game are entitled to
circulate  their]{.stl_10}

[60 ]{.stl_07}[Article 22 of the PRC ]{.stl_09}[Copyright Law.]{.stl_17
style="font-style:italic;"}

[page 31]{.stl_10}

[creation via the Internet.]{.stl_10}^[61\ ]{.stl_16}^[However, because
all copyrights incorporated within a video game, except the moral
rights, a re usually transferred to the publisher, this regulation does
not create significant additional protection for individual
authors.]{.stl_10}

[DENMARK]{.stl_11}

[75. ]{.stl_12}[Although the importance of video games has increased in
the last decade, there is still a  legislative and jurisprudential void
with regard to the legal classification of video games in  Denmark.
Creative works of authorship are protected in Denmark under the
]{.stl_10}[Consolidated  Act on Copyright of 2010]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}^[62\ ]{.stl_16}^[(hereinafter, the Danish
]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[) and,
depending on the  nature of a specific video game, it may be classified
as software, an audiovisual work, it  may have a distributive
qualification, or become a collective work. The classification
is  derived directly from the Danish ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[, Section 1, which states that:]{.stl_10}

[―(1) The person creating a literary or artistic work shall have
copyright therein, ]{.stl_19 style="font-style:italic;"}[be it expressed
in writing or in speech as a fictional or a descriptive representation,
or whether it be a musical or dramatic work, cinematographic or
photographic work, or a work of fine art, architecture, applied art, or
]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[expressed in some other
manner.‖]{.stl_19 style="font-style:italic;"}

[―(2) Maps and drawings and other works of ]{.stl_19
style="font-style:italic;"}[a descriptive nature executed in]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}

[graphic or plastic form shall be considered as literary
works.‖]{.stl_19 style="font-style:italic;"}

[―(3) Works in the form of computer programs shall be considered as
literary works.‖]{.stl_19 style="font-style:italic;"}

[76. ]{.stl_12}[Although we are not aware of any Danish jurisprudence
involving legal qualifications for  video games, the fact that Section 1
includes an open list of works of authorship (]{.stl_10}[―]{.stl_19
style="font-style:italic;"}[(...) ]{.stl_15}[ expressed in some other
manner‖)]{.stl_19 style="font-style:italic;"}[, suggests that video
games are unquestionably  protected under this law. That said any
borderline issues regarding the classification may  also rely on
jurisprudence on software and related copyright cases as, under Danish
law,  video games could bear a distributive qualification, with a
fragmentary protection of all the  elements embodied in the work
(including graphics, musical works, computer code and  audiovisual
works).]{.stl_10}

[STAKEHOLDERS INVOLVED IN THE VALUE CHAIN]{.stl_10}

[77. ]{.stl_12}[Considering the complexity of video games, there are a
great number of people involved  in the creation and exploitation of
such works of authorship, including, game developers,  the studio,
concept artists, scriptwriters, game directors and producers, game
designers,  level designers, character designers, set designers,
animators, music directors,  composers of original music, actors,
translators and code programmers. The outcome of  their work will be
protectable only if it fulfills the requirements of the
Danish  ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[,  which explicitly states that the work
must be creative and original.]{.stl_10}

[Therefore, and unlike other jurisdictions that specify who the authors
of an audiovisual work are (generally, the director, scriptwriter and
the composer of the soundtrack),]{.stl_10}

[79. ]{.stl_12}[In principle, under Danish law all contributors listed

[80. ]{.stl_12}[Recent tools and means of communication, especially the

]{.stl_10}[ ―]{.stl_15}[creation of an artistic work]{.stl_05

]{.stl_15}[residence, the law of the country in which the server is

[81. ]{.stl_12}[In order to avoid disputes with respect to the

[WHO OWNS THE RIGHTS]{.stl_10}

[82. ]{.stl_12}[With respect to the transfer of rights, Section 53 of
the Danish ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[establishes  that any copyright holder may
wholly or partially assign his or her rights under this law,  with the
exception of the above-mentioned moral rights. Accordingly, a given
assignee  shall not have the right to exploit a work in a manner or
means not initially contemplated in  the assignment agreement.
Significantly, the Danish ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[obliges assignees to  exploit the assigned
rights; authors ]{.stl_10}[may cancel the agreement with six months'
notice if ]{.stl_19 style="font-style:italic;"}[ the assignee has not
exploited the rights within three years after the date on which
the  agreement was fulfilled by the author.]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}^[66\ ]{.stl_06
style="font-style:italic;"}^[Therefore, if a studio or video game
producer  holds certain rights as a result of a transfer agreement and
that copyright holder does not  exploit the work during the period of
time since its delivery, the author shall have the right  to cancel the
assignment agreement.]{.stl_10}

[83. ]{.stl_12}[The Danish ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[establishes a specific regime for computer
programs produced  in the course of employment, holding that where a
computer program is created  by an  employee in carrying out his or her
duties or following the instructions given by the  employer, the
copyright in such a computer program shall pass to the
employer.]{.stl_10}^[67\ ]{.stl_16}^[ Therefore, unless otherwise agreed
between the parties, the author of a computer  program developed within
an employer-employee relationship shall have no copyright  in  the
outcome of that work as the Danish ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[establishes an automatic  assignment of
rights in favor of the employer. Considering the bargaining power of
each  of the parties involved in this industry, it is reasonable to
assume that, in most instances,  video game studios and producers will
own the copyright in the software developed by  their
employees.]{.stl_10}

[84. ]{.stl_12}[Therefore, the Danish ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[does not create differences in the
transfer  of rights  regime governing authors and producers with respect
to their contractual relationship, as,  in all of these cases, the law
demands an explicit transfer of rights, the only exception  being
computer programs developed under a labor relationship, where an
automatic  assignment of rights exists.]{.stl_10}

[FINANCIAL COMPENSATION]{.stl_10}

[85. ]{.stl_12}[The Danish ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[does not establish a fixed regime governing
the compensation  of authors, thereby providing flexibility to the
industry. As a consequence, in general  terms, where an
employer-employee relationship exists, the remuneration for
the  assignment of rights is included in the salary. Nonetheless, in
Denmark, incentive  schemes in the form of bonuses and distribution of
shares to employees are also  prevalent, especially at smaller
studios.]{.stl_10}

[On the other hand, for independent contractors in Denmark, in most
circumstances the compensation is a lump sum. However, some small video
game studios offer independent contractors a proportional remuneration,
in some cases combined with a moderate lump sum in order to keep the
production and development costs to a minimum.]{.stl_10}

[86. ]{.stl_12}[Therefore, Denmark does not have a mandatory scheme
governing the compensation of  authors of video games (or any other work
of authorship); however, authors generally  receive a lump sum for their
creations. In this regard, and considering that other issues  such as
the legal qualifications of video games are still unresolved, a
legislative solution  would be useful in order to bridge these gaps in
the law.]{.stl_10}

[66 ]{.stl_07}[Section 54 of the Danish ]{.stl_09}[Copyright
Act]{.stl_17 style="font-style:italic;"}[. ]{.stl_09}[67
]{.stl_07}[Section 59 of the Danish ]{.stl_09}[Copyright Act]{.stl_17
style="font-style:italic;"}[.]{.stl_09}

[page 34]{.stl_10}

[EGYPT]{.stl_11}

[87. ]{.stl_12}[Part III of Law No. 82 of 2002, ]{.stl_10}[Pertaining to
the Protection of Intellectual Property Rights ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[ (hereinafter, the Egyptian
]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[),
provides legal protection to ]{.stl_10}[any innovated work,  in the
literary, artistic or scientific domain whatever the type, manner of
expression,  significance or purpose of classification thereof.]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}^[68\ ]{.stl_06
style="font-style:italic;"}^[Although Article 140 offers an open
list  of works that can be copyrighted in Egypt (including books,
computer software, musical  works, audiovisual works, etc.), there is no
specific mention of video games  in this list or in  any other section
of this law.]{.stl_10}

[Nonetheless, it is unquestionable that, while this type of modern work
is not expressly contemplated in the Egyptian ]{.stl_10}[Copyright
Act]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[, video games can find
protection under several of the categories of works mentioned in Article
140 or, generally, in Article  138.1. Consequently, video games can be
afforded copyright protection through two means: (i) protecting the
computer program necessary to execute the audiovisual parts of the work;
and (ii) seeking protection of the user interface, as a whole in part,
including characters, musical works, scenes, settings, etc.]{.stl_10}

[Therefore, considering this distributive classification, a video game
is a complex work  that does not fit into a unique category.
Accordingly, stakeholders and rights holders will have to protect each
creative element of a given video game individually, based on the nature
of the element.]{.stl_10}

[AUTHORSHIP AND STAKEHOLDERS]{.stl_10}

[88. ]{.stl_12}[The Egyptian ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[establishes that the author of a work is the
]{.stl_10}[person who  creates the work. ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[However, video games are usually created by
more than one author,  usually in an employer-employee relationship with
a legal person who takes the initiative  and the risk to develop the
work. In this case, the Egyptian ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}^[69\ ]{.stl_16}^[establishes
]{.stl_10}[ that video games are therefore ―works of collective --
authorship‖, defined as follows:]{.stl_15}

[―The work made by more than one author under the guidance of a natural
or ]{.stl_19 style="font-style:italic;"}[juridical person, who shall
undertake publishing the work in his name and under his supervision. The
works of such authors shall be incorporated in such work, for the
general purpose aimed by such person, such that the works ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[of each author may not be separated or
distinguished independently.‖]{.stl_19 style="font-style:italic;"}

[89. ]{.stl_12}[Accordingly, the Egyptian ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act
]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[provides protection to authors,
who shall enjoy,  in respect of their work, permanent moral
rights]{.stl_10}^[70\ ]{.stl_16}^[and exclusive rights in
granting  licenses or preventing any exploitation of their works in any
manner.]{.stl_10}^[71\ ]{.stl_16}^[However, and  like in any other
jurisdiction, economic rights can be transferred or granted to any
third  party, for example in works of collective authorship, as
described above.]{.stl_10}

[90. ]{.stl_12}[In addition to publishers, distributors or retailers,
other stakeholders in the industry are  the performers who dub the
voices of video game characters, performers on the  soundtrack or, in
general, anyone who performs any creative works in any manner.  These
performers are also entitled to receive protection for their
performances, although  the economic rights are usually transferred to
the producer of the video game.]{.stl_10}

[68 ]{.stl_07}[Article 138.1 of the Egyptian ]{.stl_09}[Copyright Act.
]{.stl_17 style="font-style:italic;"}[69 ]{.stl_07}[Article 138.4 of the
Egyptian ]{.stl_09}[Copyright Act. ]{.stl_17
style="font-style:italic;"}[70 ]{.stl_07}[Article 143 of the Egyptian
]{.stl_09}[Copyright Act. ]{.stl_17 style="font-style:italic;"}[71
]{.stl_07}[Article 147 of the Egyptian ]{.stl_09}[Copyright
Act.]{.stl_17 style="font-style:italic;"}

[page 35]{.stl_10}

[TRANSFER OF RIGHTS AND COMPENSATION]{.stl_10}

[91. ]{.stl_12}[As anticipated above, authors can transfer their
economic rights in their works to any  third party, either a natural or
a legal person. According to Article 149 of the Egyptian
]{.stl_10}[ Copyright Act]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[, such
transfer must be in writing and each right granted must be  determined
in detail, including the scope, purpose, period and place of
exploitation. If a  given economic right has not been properly
transferred, then the author will keep it for  him or herself.]{.stl_10}

[92. ]{.stl_12}[In exchange for the transfer of rights, the author
should receive fair and equitable  compensation, which should be in the
form of a percentage of the income generated by  the exploitation, in a
lump-sum amount or a combination of both. Finally, Article 151 of  the
Egyptian ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[establishes a mechanism of protection for
authors whose  remuneration with respect to a work is unfairly
low:]{.stl_10}

[―Where it appears that the agreement referred to i]{.stl_19
style="font-style:italic;"}[n Article 150 is prejudicial to ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[the author's rights or became so due to
circumstances that arose after the ]{.stl_19
style="font-style:italic;"}[agreement, the author or his successor may
request the court of first instance to reconsider the value of
remuneration agreed upon, without prejudice to the ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[rights and interests of the
assignee.‖]{.stl_19 style="font-style:italic;"}

[93. ]{.stl_12}[Egypt has established a system of compulsory licenses
for educational purposes, which  has been developed based on
]{.stl_10}[Prime Ministerial Decree No. (497) of 2005 On Issuing  the
Executive Regulations for Book III of Law No. (82) of 2002 on the
Protection of  Intellectual Property Rights]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[. According to this license, described in
Article 170 of the  Egyptian ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[:]{.stl_10}

[―Any person may demand the competent Ministry to grant such person a
]{.stl_19 style="font-style:italic;"}[personal license for reproducing
and/or translating any protected work ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[pursuant to the stipulations of the law
herein, without having the author's ]{.stl_19
style="font-style:italic;"}[permission, for the purposes set forth in
the following paragraph. The grant of such license shall be against
payment of fair compensation to the author or his successors. Such
license shall not be in contradiction with the normal exploitation of
the work and does not unreasonably prejudice the legitimate ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[interests of the author or the copyright
holders.‖]{.stl_19 style="font-style:italic;"}

[―Licenses shall be granted, pursuant to a justified decision in which
the time ]{.stl_19 style="font-style:italic;"}[and place limits thereof
are specified; and for the purposes of fulfilling the ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[requirements of all kinds and levels of
education.‖]{.stl_19 style="font-style:italic;"}

[―The executive regulations of the law herein ]{.stl_19
style="font-style:italic;"}[shall define the conditions and terms
stipulated for granting licenses, as well as the categories of the due
]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[fees, which shall not exceed one
thousand Egyptian pounds for each work.‖]{.stl_19
style="font-style:italic;"}

[As per Article 5 of Prime Ministerial Decree No. (497) of 2005, the
conditions are as follows:]{.stl_10}

[―(a) The author has not withdrawn all the copies of his work from
circulation. ]{.stl_19 style="font-style:italic;"}[(b) The license is
not eligible to be assigned by the licensee to any other party. (c) The
license does not prevent issuing a license to anyone other than the
licensee, unless the license is for translating the work into a certain
language, if the translation is published in this language.]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}

[(d) The name of the author and the title of the work, or a certified
translation]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}

[thereof are mentioned on each copy.‖]{.stl_19
style="font-style:italic;"}

[page 36]{.stl_10}

[94. ]{.stl_12}[The application should be accompanied by a justification
that proves that the applicant  attempted to reach the author or its
legal representatives; that a reasonable negotiation  period lapsed
without reaching an agreement; or that the rights holders did not
make  enough copies available at a reasonable price. Finally, in order
to be eligible for this ]{.stl_10}[ license, ―]{.stl_15}[the application
shall be accompanied by sufficient evidence that proves that
the  license is required for the purpose of fulfilling the requirements
of any kind or level of  education, whether at a university, institute,
training center, or through scientific ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[ research, etc.‖.]{.stl_19
style="font-style:italic;"}^[72]{.stl_06 style="font-style:italic;"}^

[Consequently, only those involved in an education program will be
eligible to obtain such a license. Although this system is not
specifically designed for video games, it may be applicable in this area
considering the broad application of video games, which may include
educational or juvenile games.]{.stl_10}

[95. ]{.stl_12}[Finally, and as in other jurisdictions, the Egyptian
]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act ]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[protects
video games in  a distributive manner, offering protection through
different ways, including as software,  audiovisual works, or for
scripts and characters. However, and considering the  undeveloped status
of the video game industry in this country, a regulation to
explicitly  protect this kind of work is highly recommended.]{.stl_10}

[FRANCE]{.stl_11}

[CLASSIFICATION OF VIDEO GAMES]{.stl_10}

[96. ]{.stl_12}[French law, specifically the ]{.stl_10}[French Code of
Intellectual Property ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[(]{.stl_10}[Code de la
Propriété  Intellectuelle]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[)
(hereinafter, the ―]{.stl_15}[CIP]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[‖), neither provides a ]{.stl_15}[legal
classification nor a special  regime for video games. Nonetheless, video
games can find protection in the ]{.stl_10}[CIP ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[as per  Article L112-]{.stl_10}[1, which
states that ―]{.stl_15}[the provisions of this Code shall protect the
rights of  authors in all works of the mind, whatever their kind, form
of expression, merit or  purpose.]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[‖
Accordingly, Article L112]{.stl_15}[-2 includes an open list of works
that can be  protectable under the ]{.stl_10}[CIP]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[, including books, musical compositions,
graphical works and  software, among others (as the ]{.stl_10}[CIP
]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[specifies that these can be,
]{.stl_10}[in particular]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[, works of
the  mind).]{.stl_10}

[In this sense, French case law has confirmed that video games can be
considered works of the mind (]{.stl_10}[oeuvre de l'esprit]{.stl_19
style="font-style:italic;"}[) and, as such, are protected under the
general regime of copyright (]{.stl_10}[droit d'auteur]{.stl_19
style="font-style:italic;"}[).]{.stl_10}^[73\ ]{.stl_16}^[Moreover,
jurisprudence recently held that a: ―]{.stl_15}[\[...\] video game
]{.stl_19 style="font-style:italic;"}[is a complex work that cannot be
reduced to its sole software dimension, however significant it may be,
so that each of its components is governed by the legal framework
applicable to it accord]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[ing to its
nature \[...\].]{.stl_19
style="font-style:italic;"}[‖]{.stl_15}^[74]{.stl_16}^

[Under this distributive approach, a video game is considered a complex
creation which is impossible to categorize in one sole pre-existing
category, and for which each component must be subject to the legal
status applicable to it (e.g., software, music, script or
graphics).]{.stl_10}

[72 ]{.stl_07}[Article 6 of Prime Ministerial Decree No. (497) of
2005.]{.stl_09}

[72 ]{.stl_07}[Cass. Ass. Plén., 7 mars 1986, ]{.stl_09}[Atari Inc. c/
Valadon]{.stl_17 style="font-style:italic;"}[, pourvoi
n°84-93509.]{.stl_09}

[74 ]{.stl_07}[Cass. 1re civ., June 25, 2009, ]{.stl_09}[Lefranc c/ Sté
SESAM]{.stl_17 style="font-style:italic;"}[, pourvoi n°07-20387; CA
Paris, September 26, 2011,]{.stl_09}

[Pôle 5, Chambre 12, ]{.stl_09}[SARL AAKRO PURE TRONIC et a. c/

[page 37]{.stl_10}

[97. ]{.stl_12}[A recent study]{.stl_10}^[75\ ]{.stl_16}^[on video
games, commissioned by the French National Assembly,  concluded that
video game litigation is rare and that such a fragmented legal status
does  not call for the creation of a special definition and regime for
video games in France. The  study also suggested that copyright rules
(]{.stl_10}[droit d'auteur]{.stl_19 style="font-style:italic;"}[) should
be modified, after  discussing the relevant changes with rights holders
and stakeholders, to take into account  the specificity of these modern
works.]{.stl_10}

[RIGHTS HOLDERS AND STAKEHOLDERS]{.stl_10}

[98. ]{.stl_12}[Therefore, it is also necessary to determine who can be
deemed the ]{.stl_10}[authors ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[of  a video  game and the stakeholders
involved in this growing industry in order to consider the legal  nature
of this kind of work. According to business practice and law, the main
stakeholders  are the publishers (]{.stl_10}[éditeurs]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[), the development studios
(]{.stl_10}[studios de développement]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[) and  the authors
(]{.stl_10}[auteurs]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[, i.e.,
individuals working as employees or as
freelancers/independent  contractors for development studios or
publishers). In this regard, there are different  elements implied in
the process; hence the question of which of these contributors can
be  qualified as authors must be addressed.]{.stl_10}

[In France, any natural person who contributes, totally or partially, to
the creation of a video game can be qualified as an author, as long as
his/her contribution is creative and original, as defined by relevant
jurisprudence (i.e., stamped with the personality of its author).
Inevitably, this requires a case-by-case analysis, as courts have ruled
that, based on the context a sound designer can be considered the author
of various sounds and music created specifically for an online video
game.]{.stl_10}^[76]{.stl_16}^

[99. ]{.stl_12}[According to the above-mentioned study on video games by
the French National  Assembly, experts and stakeholders consider that
the lead game designers, art directors,  sound designers and
scriptwriters are the contributors most likely to be considered  authors
due to their involvement in the creative
process.]{.stl_10}^[77\ ]{.stl_06
style="font-style:italic;"}^[Nevertheless, many other  individuals can
be involved in the creative process of a video game and thus
generate  copyrights, including the character and setting designers and
the programmers.]{.stl_10}

[100. ]{.stl_12}[Additionally, people not directly involved in the
creation of the video game may become  authors of part of the video game
or of its elements. This is the case with players involved  in
interactive online gaming, which can create, in certain games, settings,
characters,  cars  or any other element that could also become available
for other players. Such interactivity  has become very popular in recent
years; however, the laws of different countries have  not yet captured
this development.]{.stl_10}

[In France, the legal status of the contributions by players involved in
interactive online gaming is neither specifically defined by law nor by
case law. Potentially, such players could be considered authors of their
own contributions (e.g., customized items in the game environment) and,
therefore, vested with the copyrights (]{.stl_10}[droit
d'auteur]{.stl_19 style="font-style:italic;"}[)  in such contributions,
provided that these qualify as works of the mind (]{.stl_10}[oeuvre de
l'esprit]{.stl_19 style="font-style:italic;"}[), i.e., ]{.stl_10}[show
―originality‖ as defined by case law by the mark of the author's
personality or his/her ]{.stl_15}[personal intellectual or artistic
contribution, as well as by the existence of a creative effort. Any
exploitation of this user-generated content would require proper
authorization, which, in these virtual scenarios, is usually obtained
through an end-user license agreement that the player must accept when
opening an account on the system.]{.stl_10}

[75 ]{.stl_07}[―]{.stl_08}[Mission Parlementaire sur le Régime
Juridiq]{.stl_09}[ue du Jeu Vidéo en Droit d'Auteur‖, report by
M]{.stl_08}[. Patrice Martin-]{.stl_09}

[Lalande, November 2011, Ref. 114000733.]{.stl_09}

[THE QUESTION OF THE RIGHTS]{.stl_10}

[101. ]{.stl_12}[Considering the complexity of this kind of work of
authorship, the question of who owns  the copyright in the final game,
and in each and every one of the elements that are part of  the work, is
not trivial. Among all the elements concerned in the process, some can
be  regulated by a labor relationship, which raises the issue of who is
considered the author in  an employer-employee relationship, while
others are created by freelancers or third-party  companies.]{.stl_10}

[In this regard, according to French law, an employee can be considered
an ]{.stl_10}[author]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[,  even though
he/she is acting under the authority of an
employer.]{.stl_10}^[78\ ]{.stl_16}^[Another essential aspect of the
creative process concerns the different regimes applicable to the
transfer of rights between them, in particular between authors,
producers and publishers.]{.stl_10}

[In light of the distributive approach (]{.stl_10}[see the second
paragraph of this section]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[), all
different regimes outlined below may be applicable to the transfer of
patrimonial rights between authors, publishers and development
studios.]{.stl_10}

[102. ]{.stl_12}[The general rule is that the transfer of such
copyrights must be done through a contract  between authors, development
studios and publishers, in which specific elements must be  included in
contracts with authors. In this sense, Article L.131-3 of the
]{.stl_10}[CIP ]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[requires
that:]{.stl_10}

[―]{.stl_15}[Transfer of authors' rights shall be subject to each of the
assigned rights ]{.stl_19 style="font-style:italic;"}[being separately
mentioned in the instrument of assignment and with the field of
exploitation of the assigned rights being defined as to its scope and
purpose, the territory and the duration.]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[‖]{.stl_15}

[As an exception, the transfer of copyrights is automatic for software
(a component of video games) between an employee, legal author of such
software, and his or her employer. Accordingly, Article L.113-9 of the
]{.stl_10}[CIP ]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[provides
that:]{.stl_10}

[―Unless otherwise provided by statutory provision or stipulation, the
economic ]{.stl_19 style="font-style:italic;"}[rights in the software
and its documentation created by one or more employees in the execution
of their duties or following the instructions given by their employer
shall be the property of the employer and he exclusively shall ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[be entitled to exercise them.‖]{.stl_19
style="font-style:italic;"}

[Another exception is for collective works (]{.stl_10}[oeuvre
collective]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[),]{.stl_10}^[79\ ]{.stl_16}^[where the
producer or the publisher is deemed the original owner of the copyrights
in such works, as established in Article L113-5 of the
]{.stl_10}[CIP]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[:]{.stl_10}

[―A collective work shall be the property, unless proved otherwise, of
the ]{.stl_19 style="font-style:italic;"}[natural or legal person under
whose name it has been disclosed. ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[The author's rights shall vest in such
person.]{.stl_19 style="font-style:italic;"}[‖]{.stl_15}

[One final exception concerns audiovisual
works,]{.stl_10}^[80\ ]{.stl_16}^[where a presumption of authorship
exists for a list of persons (i.e., the scriptwriter, director and
author of the musical]{.stl_10}

[78 ]{.stl_07}[This principle is contained  in Article L111-1, paragraph
3,  which states that: ]{.stl_09}[―]{.stl_08}[The existence
or  conclusion of a]{.stl_17 style="font-style:italic;"}

[contract for hire or  of service by the author of  a work of the mind
shall in  no way derogate from the enjoyment  of the]{.stl_17
style="font-style:italic;"}

[right afforded by the first paragraph.]{.stl_17
style="font-style:italic;"}[‖ (]{.stl_08}[This paragraph refers to the
]{.stl_09}[exclusive incorporeal  property right ]{.stl_17
style="font-style:italic;"}[of authors.). ]{.stl_09}[79 ]{.stl_20
style="font-style:italic;"}[According to  Article L113-2:
]{.stl_09}[―]{.stl_18 style="font-style:italic;"}[c]{.stl_17
style="font-style:italic;"}[ollective  work‖ shall  ]{.stl_18
style="font-style:italic;"}[mean a work  created at the  initiative of
a  natural or legal]{.stl_17 style="font-style:italic;"}

[person who  edits, publishes and  discloses it  under  his
or  her  direction  and  name  and  in  which  the  personal
contributions of  the various authors  who participated in
its  production are merged  in the overall  work for which  they were
conceived, without it being possible to attribute to each author a
separate right in the work created.]{.stl_17 style="font-style:italic;"}

[page 39]{.stl_10}

[composition) and a presumption of transfer of their patrimonial rights
exists for the]{.stl_10}

[producer, as per Article L.132-24 of the ]{.stl_10}[CIP]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[:]{.stl_10}

[―Contracts binding the producer and the authors of an audiovisual work,
other ]{.stl_19 style="font-style:italic;"}[than the author of a musical
composition with or without words, shall imply, unless otherwise
stipulated and notwithstanding the rights afforded to the author by
Articles L111-3, L121-4, L121-5, L122-1 to L122-7, L123-7, L131-2 to
L131-7, L132-4 and L132-7, assignment to the producer of the exclusive
exploi]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[tation rights in the
audiovisual work.‖]{.stl_19 style="font-style:italic;"}

[―Audiovisual production contracts shall not imply assignment to the
producer of the graphic rights and theatrical rights in the
work.‖]{.stl_19 style="font-style:italic;"}

[―Contracts shall lay down the list of those elements that have served
to make]{.stl_19 style="font-style:italic;"}

[t]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[he work which are to be
conserved as well as the conditions of conservation.‖]{.stl_19
style="font-style:italic;"}

[103. ]{.stl_12}[Finally, moral rights (such as the right of
publication, the right to be named as author and  to prevent
modification/alteration of the work) are always retained by the authors
and  cannot be transferred or waived, regardless of the contractual
relationship between the  parties. Moreover, while patrimonial rights
apply only for a limited time (until 70 years  after the death of the
author), moral rights are perpetual and are transferred to the heirs
of  the author after his or her death or to the persons listed as
beneficiaries in the will.]{.stl_10}^[81]{.stl_16}^

[104. ]{.stl_12}[Consequently, while it is customary in the video game
industry to expressly state in  licenses and/or written agreements the
transfer of rights for any contribution to the video  game, the
effectiveness of the transfer will depend on the regime applicable to
the part of  the video game at stake.]{.stl_10}

[COMPENSATION]{.stl_10}

[105. ]{.stl_12}[Another substantial aspect of the transfer of rights
concerns the different kinds of  financial  compensation available for
authors of video games. The general rule applicable in France  is, with
respect to the assignment of copyrights, that authors (whether an
employee or  independent contractor/freelancer) are entitled to
compensation in the form of proportional  remuneration, unless they fall
under one of the exceptions to the general rule where a  lump sum is
permissible, per Article L.131-4 of the ]{.stl_10}[CIP]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[, namely, in the following cases:]{.stl_10}

[―1°]{.stl_19 style="font-style:italic;"}[. The basis for calculating
the proportional participation cannot be practically]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}

[determined;]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}

[2°. The means of supervising the participation are lacking;]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}

[3°. The cost of the calculation and supervising operations would be out
of  proportion with the expected results;]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}

[\[Footnote continued from previous page\]]{.stl_21}

[80 ]{.stl_07}[The ]{.stl_09}[CIP  ]{.stl_17
style="font-style:italic;"}[establishes that  an audiovisual  work
shall  be a  ]{.stl_09}[work of  collaboration]{.stl_17
style="font-style:italic;"}[, as  only natural persons can]{.stl_09}

[claim authorship in such works,  and the creators of such films shall

[106. ]{.stl_12}[Given the particular nature of video games, the number
of people involved in their  creation, the partial contribution of each
author and the business practices in this industry,  one can conclude
that a remuneration scheme based on royalties should be
withdrawn.  Nevertheless, if the compensation received by the author is
manifestly low, the affected  creator could demand a review of the price
conditions as per Article L131-5 of the ]{.stl_10}[CIP.]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}^[82]{.stl_16}^

[107. ]{.stl_12}[Therefore, questions as to the legal classification of
video games, the regimes  applicable  to the transfer of rights and the
different kinds of financial compensation available for  authors must
still be addressed by French legislation. In this regard, it is
important to note  that the French National Assembly recently discussed
these questions; however, this work  has not progressed further since
the last national elections.]{.stl_10}

[GERMANY]{.stl_11}

[108. ]{.stl_12}[The ]{.stl_10}[Gesetz uber Urheberrecht und verwandte
Schutzrechte ]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[-- ]{.stl_19
style="font-style:italic;"}[Urheberrechtsgesetz ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[-- ]{.stl_19

]{.stl_10}[-- ]{.stl_15}[Copyright Law) (hereinafter ]{.stl_10}[the
―]{.stl_15}[UrhG]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[‖),  was
]{.stl_15}[ enacted in 1965 and has been modified several times since,
with the last major  amendment in 2008. As in other jurisdictions, this
law provides protection to authors of  literary, scientific and artistic
works (§ 1 of the ]{.stl_10}[UrhG]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[), which include works of  language  and
computer programs,]{.stl_10}^[83\ ]{.stl_16}^[musical
works,]{.stl_10}^[84\ ]{.stl_16}^[works of fine arts, architecture and
plans of  such works,]{.stl_10}^[85\ ]{.stl_16}^[photographic works,
including works produced by processes similar
to  cinematography,]{.stl_10}^[86\ ]{.stl_16}^[and drawings, plans, maps
and sketches.]{.stl_10}^[87\ ]{.stl_16}^[There is no reference to  video
games ]{.stl_10}[as such ]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[in this
law; nonetheless, the list of works provided by § 2 of the
]{.stl_10}[ UrhG ]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[is
]{.stl_10}[numerus apertus ]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[and, as
a consequence, other works like video games and  multimedia works can
also find protection within the law. Finally, this section ends by
]{.stl_10}[ stating that: ―]{.stl_15}[personal intellectual creations
alone shall constitute works within the ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[ meaning of this law‖ ]{.stl_19
style="font-style:italic;"}[(§ 2 II of the ]{.stl_10}[UrhG]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[)]{.stl_10}[.]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}

[CLASSIFICATION OF VIDEO GAMES]{.stl_10}

[109. ]{.stl_12}[Considering that the ]{.stl_10}[UrhG ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[establishes no specific rules for
classification of video games,  legal doctrine considers them to be
multimedia works. Therefore, different classifications  apply to the
protection of video games within the ]{.stl_10}[UrhG]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[.]{.stl_10}

[The computer program that controls the game and underlies the
audiovisual work is categorized as a ]{.stl_10}[speech work ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[(§ 2 I Nr. 1 of the ]{.stl_10}[UrhG]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[). In this regard, and as all video games
are constructed with computer code that enables their execution in a
computer system, Section VIII of Part I of the ]{.stl_10}[UrhG ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[applies.]{.stl_10}

[Generally, §§ 69a ff. of the ]{.stl_10}[UrhG ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[establishes the legal regime of computer
programs, ]{.stl_10}[protecting exclusively ―]{.stl_15}[the expression
in any form of a computer program‖]{.stl_19
style="font-style:italic;"}[, where this is original.
]{.stl_10}[Consequently, ―]{.stl_15}[ideas and principles that underlie
any element of a computer ]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[program,
including those which underlie its interfaces, shall not be
protected‖.]{.stl_19 style="font-style:italic;"}^[88]{.stl_16}^

[110. ]{.stl_12}[The audiovisual presentation of the video game is
treated as a ]{.stl_10}[film work ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[(§ 2 I Nr. 5 of the
]{.stl_10}[ UrhG]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[), the regime for
which is further developed in Section I of Part III of the
]{.stl_10}[UrhG.]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}^[89  ]{.stl_16}^[In  order to benefit from
the protection granted, film works shall be personal
intellectual  creations according to the terms of § 2 II of the
]{.stl_10}[UrhG]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[. Personal
intellectual creations  require that the collective work of all
contributors (e.g., game designers, animation and  graphic artists and
sound engineers) using film-like methods achieves a certain level
of  artistic creation. If the work does not attain this level of
originality and creativity, ]{.stl_10}[ jurisprudence protects the
audiovisual presentation of a video game at least as
―]{.stl_15}[moving  images]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[‖,]{.stl_15}^[90\ ]{.stl_16}^[which do not
require proof of personal intellectual
creation.]{.stl_10}^[91]{.stl_16}^

[RIGHTS HOLDERS AND STAKEHOLDERS]{.stl_10}

of]{.stl_15}

[complex scenarios involving the stakeholders and rights holders of
video games.]{.stl_10}

[Accordingly, when analyzing the different owners of copyrights in a
video game, one must first review who has contributed to the creation of
the work by providing original and creative elements. Consequently,
there can be innumerable contributors to a video game, including concept
artists, character designers, scriptwriters, argument writers, game
directors, set and plans designers, music composers, programmers and
actors. Therefore, all of these parties, and any others whose
contribution can be deemed original and creative, may have rights in the
final work.]{.stl_10}

[In this regard, if several persons contribute equally to the creation
of a video game, they are co-authors and their respective contributions
cannot be separately exploited.]{.stl_10}^[92\ ]{.stl_16}^[Therefore,
the rights of publication and of exploitation of the work shall belong
jointly to the joint authors or the person who has acquired their
exploitation rights by law or contract, as described below.]{.stl_10}

[112. ]{.stl_12}[Concerning computer programs, the authors are the
persons who make a creative  contribution to the process of software
engineering. The ]{.stl_10}[UrhG ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[affirms that, where  software is created by

with the authors.]{.stl_10}^[94]{.stl_16}^

[INDIA]{.stl_11}

[LACK OF A SPECIFIC CLASSIFICATION]{.stl_10}

[117. ]{.stl_12}[There is no regulated video game classification or
censorship in India. Since gaming law  in India is not fully developed,
the legal classification derives from business practice and is  based on
the technicalities of each specific
case.]{.stl_10}^[101\ ]{.stl_16}^[Moreover, the Indian
]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act of  1957 ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[(hereinafter, the Indian
]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[)
establishes, at its Preliminary section, the  different definitions
a]{.stl_10}[nd interpretations according to which ―]{.stl_15}[artistic
work means: (i)  a]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}

17.]{.stl_09}

[100 ]{.stl_07}[Schricker/Loewenheim, Urheberrecht § 31 Nr.
27.]{.stl_09}

[101 ]{.stl_07}[As the study on ]{.stl_09}[―]{.stl_08}[Creating Virtual
Wealth: Importance of Intellectual Property in the Animation &
Gaming]{.stl_09}

[Industry]{.stl_09}[‖ ]{.stl_08}[by Symbiosis Law School, Noida and
Scriboard, New Delhi, explains that the Indian animation  and gaming
industry has played ]{.stl_09}[a seminal role in developing India's
domestic ]{.stl_08}[entertainment and media  industry.  In 2011, it was
estimated that the Indian animation industry would grow at a compound
annual growth rate (CAGR) of  49 per cent by 2012. Moreover, this growth
rate should be accompanied by an investor-friendly regulatory
environment  that will help fuel the required investment in the sector.
Weak intellectual property regulation discourages animation and gaming
companies in India from producing their own intellectual property,
although the Indian laws  governing intellectual property rights are
compliant with world standards.]{.stl_09}

[painting, a sculpture, a drawing, an engraving or a photograph, whether

[KEY STAKEHOLDERS]{.stl_10}

[119. ]{.stl_12}[The development of a given video game is undertaken by
a game developer, which might  be a single person or a large enterprise.
The main stakeholders involved in the value  chain and the development
process include:]{.stl_10}

[a. ]{.stl_10}[Producer: A producer's responsibilities include
management of the development]{.stl_15}

[team, maintenance of budget and quality assurance.]{.stl_10}

[b. Publisher: A company that publishes video games that it has itself
made, or for  which it has procured development or acquired the
distribution rights.]{.stl_10}

[c. Development Team, which may include:]{.stl_10}

[i. ]{.stl_12}[Artist: The art director manages the art team comprising
visual artists who]{.stl_10}

[create video game art.]{.stl_10}

[The video game therefore contains several parts that, when combined,
constitute the final product: the game code, the characters, the
dialogue, audio/music, the video and the storyline. All those elements
are individually copyrightable according to the Indian

[AUTHORS AND THE TRANSFER OF RIGHTS]{.stl_10}

[120. ]{.stl_12}[In mobile or online gaming, the producers typically
have full rights and therefore  do not  share most of the revenue. The
main content developer can qualify as an author, along  with the team
responsible for setting up the theme of the game. Section 2 (d) (vi) of
the  Indian ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[enunciates the meaning of an
―]{.stl_15}[author]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[‖ in
]{.stl_15}[relation to any literary,  dramatic, musical or artistic work
that is computer-generated, as the person who causes  the work to be
created. Therefore, in the case of video games, authorship will vest in
the  producer or publisher (as the case may be) that causes the game to
be created, even if  that development includes creative contributions
from employees or third-party  contractors.]{.stl_10}

[This principle is reinforced by other provisions of the Indian
]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[. Chapter
IV ]{.stl_10}[-- ]{.stl_15}[―Ownership of Copyright and the Rights of
the Owner‖ ]{.stl_19 style="font-style:italic;"}[--
]{.stl_15}[establishes that in certain cases (]{.stl_10}[employment by
the proprietor of a newspaper, magazine or similar periodical under a
contract of service or apprenticeship; photograph taken, or a painting
or portrait drawn, or an engraving or a cin]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[ematograph film; or a work made in the
course of the author's ]{.stl_19 style="font-style:italic;"}[employment
under a contract of service or apprenticeship]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[), the person who arranged all the elements
to obtain the creation of such a work shall be its author and, thus, the
first owner of the copyright in the work.]{.stl_10}^[107]{.stl_06
style="font-style:italic;"}^

[Nonetheless, this principle applies in the absence of any agreement to
the contrary, as per Section 17 of the Indian ]{.stl_10}[Copyright
Act]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[. In this regard, in the
absence of a contract of employment, the original creators (i.e., the
development team) who conceived the basic ]{.stl_10}[idea and
transformed it into an entire game would qualify as ―authors‖ under the
Indian ]{.stl_15}[Copyright Act ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[and would be entitled to authorship
rights.]{.stl_10}

[121. ]{.stl_12}[In order to determine whether a person is engaged in ―a
contract of service‖ or ―contract  for service‖ it is necessary to
consider whether that person is rendering the services as a
]{.stl_15}[ person in business on his or her own account. If the answer
is affirmative, then the  contract is a contract ]{.stl_10}[for
]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[service; if not, the contract is a
contract ]{.stl_10}[of ]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[service.
The proper  test to ascertain if such a relationship exists is whether
or not the employer has the right to  control the manner of execution of
the work. However, ]{.stl_10}[control ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[in itself is not always  conclusive and
factors like the degree of control, opportunities of profit or loss,
investment]{.stl_10}

[106 ]{.stl_07}[Study on ]{.stl_09}[―Creating Virtual Wealth: Importance
of Intellectual Property in the Animation & Gaming Industry‖]{.stl_08}[,
by]{.stl_09}

[Symbiosis Law School, Noida and Scriboard, New Delhi.]{.stl_09}

[107 ]{.stl_07}[Section 17 of the Indian ]{.stl_09}[Copyright
Ac]{.stl_17 style="font-style:italic;"}[.]{.stl_09}

[page 46]{.stl_10}

[in facilities, permanency of relations and skills required in the
claimed independent operation also play a significant
role.]{.stl_10}^[108]{.stl_16}^

[122. ]{.stl_12}[Section 18 of the Indian ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act
]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[affirms that a copyright owner may
assign the rights  in an existing work to any person, either wholly or
partially, generally or subject to  limitations, and for the whole term
of the copyright or any part thereof. As per Section 19,  only written,
signed assignments are valid, and they must also include the
identification of  the work, the duration and the territorial scope of
the assignment; therefore, verbal  or  unsigned documents are null
according to the Indian ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[. In the absence of a  time period or
territorial scope, the assignment shall be limited to a term of five
years  within the geographical area of India.]{.stl_10}

[123. ]{.stl_12}[As video games have become more sophisticated, a new
problem has arisen involving  contributions by online game players.
Indian law has yet to address the specific legal  issues of interactive
online gaming. However, as the behavior of avatars becomes
more  realistic, sophisticated and intelligent, the question regarding
the legal status of the  contributions made by players may give rise to
disputes. Conferring on the players  exclusive rights to their creations
and contributions in a game might add a new dimension  to the world of
gaming. ]{.stl_10}[The players' contributions would then become their
property that ]{.stl_15}[ can be bought, sold or licensed like any other
property.]{.stl_10}

[ECONOMIC COMPENSATION FOR AUTHORS]{.stl_10}

[124. ]{.stl_12}[Compensation for authors by copyright owner employers
is governed by the employment ]{.stl_10}[ agreement and the
organization's/employer's company rules, and may include a bonus or
]{.stl_15}[ another form of payment as agreed upon by the parties. Here
again, it is pertinent  whether the developer of the video game is an
individual working as a sole proprietor or  an employee bound by an
employment contract.]{.stl_10}

[In India, royalty payments are, in most cases, not a part of the
financial compensation paid to video game creators, even though Section
19.(3) of the Indian ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[states that the assignment of copyright in
any work shall also specify the amount of royalty payable, if any, to
the author or his or her legal heirs.]{.stl_10}

[125. ]{.stl_12}[Currently, producers of cinematographic works hold all
rights, while contributors like music  composers do not receive
royalties once a song or music has been incorporated in the  work. This
is the position following the decision of the Supreme Court in its
landmark  judgment in ]{.stl_10}[Indian Performing Rights Society Ltd.
v. Eastern India Motion Pictures  Association ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[(the ]{.stl_10}[IPRS Case]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[).]{.stl_10}^[109\ ]{.stl_16}^[In the
]{.stl_10}[IPRS Case]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[, the
Copyright Board initially decided  that composers and lyricists retained
copyright in their musical works incorporated as  soundtracks in
cinematograph films and thus could collect fees, royalties and charges
with  respect to those films. On appeal, the High Court set aside the
decision of the Board.  Finally, the Supreme Court held that
interpreting Section 17(b) and (c) in terms of Section  13(4) meant that
the rights of the music composer and lyricist were defeated by virtue
of  the producer becoming the first owner of the copyright. If the
author of a lyric or musical  work authorized a film producer to make a
cinematographic ]{.stl_10}[film using the author's
]{.stl_15}[ composition, the author cannot later claim copyright
infringement.]{.stl_10}

[However, the recent proposed amendment to the Indian
]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act ]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[is
directed towards providing exclusive rights to authors/performers and
introduces moral rights for them additionally. The Bill proposes to
insert Section 38A and 38B, replacing Section 38(3) and]{.stl_10}

[108 ]{.stl_07}[As held by  the Supreme Court in  ]{.stl_09}[Silver
Jubilee Tailoring House  and Others v. Chief Inspector of  Shops
and]{.stl_17 style="font-style:italic;"}

[Establishments and Another, ]{.stl_17 style="font-style:italic;"}[1974
AIR 37, 1974 SCR (1) 747.]{.stl_09}

[109 ]{.stl_07}[1977 AIR 1443, 1977 SCR (3) 206.]{.stl_09}

[page 47]{.stl_10}

[(4), to establish that once the performer has consented to the
incorporation of the performance in a cinematograph film (work), the
performer cannot object to the enjoyment ]{.stl_10}[of the performer's
rights by the producer.]{.stl_15}^[110\ ]{.stl_16}^[However, the
performer will still be entitled  to royalties from the commercial use
of the performance.]{.stl_10}

[It is unclear whether this new provision will affect video game authors
due to the lack of qualification of this kind of work of authorship;
this amendment to the Indian  ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[must therefore be further interpreted in
this context. Additionally, India follows an Anglo- American tradition,
permitting that non-natural persons can become
]{.stl_10}[authors]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[; therefore,
video game studios will generally be the authors and copyright owners of
such works of authorship. Nonetheless, the new ]{.stl_10}[Copyright
(Amendment) Act of 2012 ]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[must be
interpreted by Indian courts in order to determine if it will apply to
video game contributors and whether they shall have the right to receive
royalties for the exploitation of their works.]{.stl_10}

[ISRAEL]{.stl_11}

[126. ]{.stl_12}[The legal standards regarding video games in Israel
stem from court judgments.  However, to date these judgments have been
somewhat inconsistent and appear to be  heavily influenced by the
particular merits and circumstances of each case. Furthermore,  the fact
that certain judgments have been rendered by split decisions of judicial
panels  emphasizes the complexity of the issues under Israeli
law.]{.stl_10}

[CLASSIFICATION OF VIDEO GAMES]{.stl_10}

[127. ]{.stl_12}[According to the ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Law of 2007
]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[(hereinafter, the Israeli
]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[),
copyright  shall subsist in original works that are literary works,
artistic works, dramatic works  or  musical works, fixed in any form;
and in sound recordings.]{.stl_10}^[111\ ]{.stl_06
style="font-style:italic;"}^[The Israeli ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act
]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[ does not offer, like the law in
other countries, an open list of works that deserve protection  under
this law; however, video games can be copyrighted in Israel pursuant to
the above-  mentioned Section 4.]{.stl_10}

[The Israeli ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[does not offer a separate and specific
regime for audiovisual works, nor for audiovisual recordings, as it only
mentions cinematographic works in the ]{.stl_10}[first section
(―Definitions‖), in defining ―dramatic works‖ as follows:
―]{.stl_15}[including  plays, cinematographic works,
musical-dramati]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[c works,
choreography, and pantomime,‖ ]{.stl_19
style="font-style:italic;"}[after ]{.stl_10}[which it specifically
identifies the term ―cinematographic works‖ as ―]{.stl_15}[including a
television work and any work which is substantially similar to a
cinematographic work or a television work.]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[‖]{.stl_15}

[Therefore, video games are protected in Israel mainly as computer
programs, which are ]{.stl_10}[considered ―]{.stl_15}[literary
works‖]{.stl_19 style="font-style:italic;"}[. ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[The definition of ―computer program‖ is also
brief, including ―]{.stl_15}[computer program in any form of
expression.‖ ]{.stl_19 style="font-style:italic;"}[However, the
]{.stl_10}[Computer Act of 1995 ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[defines a program as a group of orders in
computer language that is able to cause the functioning of a computer or
to prompt a computer action, and that is embedded, incorporated or
marked in an apparatus or object by electronic, electromagnetic,
electrochemical, electro-optical or other means, or is incorporated or
integrated in a computer in any way or that is separate from a
computer.]{.stl_10}

[128. ]{.stl_12}[In light of the above, video games, as a whole, are
mainly protected as computer]{.stl_10}

[programs in Israel, although one can seek protection of the individual
elements of a given]{.stl_10}

[110 ]{.stl_07}[Section 38A(2) to be inserted by the
]{.stl_09}[Copyright (Amendment) Act of 2012]{.stl_17
style="font-style:italic;"}[, available at]{.stl_09}

Act]{.stl_17 style="font-style:italic;"}[.]{.stl_09}

[video game as a dramatic work, provided it fulfills the requirements of
