[Israeli ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[.]{.stl_10}

[RIGHTS HOLDERS AND STAKEHOLDERS]{.stl_10}

[129. ]{.stl_12}[The Israeli ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[does not define an ―author/creator‖ nor does
it define what could ]{.stl_15}[ be considered a creation. Even where
]{.stl_10}[authors ]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[are mentioned
in the law (e.g., in relation  to joint works), the text does not offer
a definition of this concept, nor does the law specify  in which
circumstances a natural (or a legal) person can be deemed an
]{.stl_10}[author.]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}

[Therefore, in the absence of a proper legal framework, one must seek
answers in the context of business practice and in the courts. The
stakeholders involved in the value chain or in the chain of rights are
defined differently by the courts in certain cases, taking into account
the circumstances and merits of each case. The courts base their
decision on two main criteria:]{.stl_10}

[i. ]{.stl_12}[a creator must have made a significant contribution to
the creation; and]{.stl_10}

[ii. ]{.stl_12}[the quality of the contribution must be
significant.]{.stl_10}

[The decisions of Israeli courts in this area of law are not entirely
consistent. In certain cases the courts have held that a significant
contribution to the creation is required in order to recognize someone
as a stakeholder in the value and/or rights chain, even if the
contribution is not a significant technical one. However, in other cases
the courts have insisted that the significant contribution must include
a technical contribution.]{.stl_10}

[130. ]{.stl_12}[Finally, as the legal status of contributions by video
game players has yet to be defined in  the Israeli ]{.stl_10}[Copyright
Act]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[, this issue has to be agreed
upon contractually, on a case-by-  case basis or, with respect to online
platforms, according to the terms and conditions set  forth by game
operators.]{.stl_10}

[In light of the apparent inconsistencies in the court decisions, it is
not possible to provide a clear answer to the question of authorship
given that, in Israel, this must currently be determined on a
case-by-case basis.]{.stl_10}

[TRANSFER OF RIGHTS]{.stl_10}

[131. ]{.stl_12}[According to Section 33 of the Israeli
]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act, ]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[the
―]{.stl_15}[author‖ ]{.stl_19 style="font-style:italic;"}[is the first
owner of the  copyright in the work, while the producer of a sound
recording is the first owner of the  copyright in a sound recording.
According to Section 34 of the Israeli ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[, an  employer is the first owner of a
copyright related to a work created by an employee  through the services
rendered by that employee in the course of employment. The  employee is
the original creator of the work, although the law presumes that
ownership of  the exploitation rights will vest in the employer unless
it has been otherwise agreed upon  between the parties.]{.stl_10}

[Nonetheless, when a video game studio hires a freelancer to develop
specific elements of a given video game, the law presumes that the first
owner of the copyrights will be the author, unless otherwise so agreed
between the commissioning party and the author, expressly or
impliedly.]{.stl_10}^[112\ ]{.stl_16}^[Therefore, there is no automatic
transfer of rights between the company and the author, and any right
shall be transferred either expressly through a written assignment, or
impliedly, in a similar agreement.]{.stl_10}

[112 ]{.stl_07}[Section 35 of the Israeli ]{.stl_09}[Copyright
Act]{.stl_17 style="font-style:italic;"}[.]{.stl_09}

[page 49]{.stl_10}

[132. ]{.stl_12}[In this same regard, the Israeli ]{.stl_10}[Copyright
Act ]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[recognizes certain moral
rights of authors,  emphasizing that they are personal and
non-transferable, which vest in authors even  when he or she has
transferred his or her rights to a third
party.]{.stl_10}^[113\ ]{.stl_16}^[Nonetheless, regarding  infringement
of moral rights, Section 50 of the Israeli ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act
]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[specifies
that  certain  ac]{.stl_10}[ts: ―]{.stl_15}[shall not constitute an
infringement of the said moral right where the act was  reasonable in
the circumstances of the case]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[,
including ]{.stl_10}[that the work had been made by  an employee in the
course of his employment or pursuant to commission]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[.‖ This does not ]{.stl_15}[ necessarily
mean that where an employer-employee relationship exists, or in cases
of  service agreements, moral rights can be infringed, but that the
particular circumstances of  the case must be analyzed by the
courts.]{.stl_10}

[133. ]{.stl_12}[The transfer of rights from the aforementioned rights
holders is outlined in Section 37 of  the Israeli ]{.stl_10}[Copyright
Act]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[, which sets forth the
conditions applicable to the transfer of rights, ]{.stl_10}[ inter
alia]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[, as follows:]{.stl_10}

[a. Copyrights may be assigned by contract or under a legal obligation,
and the owner  may grant an exclusive license or a non-exclusive license
with respect to the  copyrights.]{.stl_10}

[b. Assignment of the copyrights or the grant of a license, as stated in
subsection (a),  above, may refer to the copyright in whole or in part,
and can be limited to a certain  territory, period of time or to
specific acts with respect to the work. c. A contract for the assignment
of copyright or the grant of an exclusive license  therein shall require
a written document.]{.stl_10}

[134. ]{.stl_12}[Regarding remuneration, the Israeli
]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act ]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[is also
brief in this sense, making no  mention of remuneration or royalties in
favor of authors or producers. In certain cases,  courts have held that
the employee was entitled to royalties or another form of  compensation
in respect of the contribution/creation.]{.stl_10}

[Therefore, compensation arrangements may vary on a case-by-case basis.
The employment agreement may provide that the salary includes any
compensation with respect to creation of copyrights and intellectual
property rights. This provision must be drafted carefully according to
the guidelines set forth in the decisions of the labor tribunals.
]{.stl_10}[If the employee makes a creation ―]{.stl_15}[in the course of
his service and during the period of his service]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[‖ (Sectio]{.stl_15}[n 34 of the Israeli
]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[), the
employee's salary may ]{.stl_15}[be considered financial compensation
for the waiver of rights.]{.stl_10}

[135. ]{.stl_12}[With respect to creations by independent contractors,
according to Section 35 of the  Israeli ]{.stl_10}[Copyright
Act]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[, compensation should be agreed
upon in the contract between the  parties and may comprise compensation
in a fixed amount, royalties, a combination of  both or any other form
of compensation.]{.stl_10}

[136. ]{.stl_12}[The Israeli ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[is not detailed with regard to the
protection of works of  authorship. Video games are not specifically
referenced, nor does the Israeli ]{.stl_10}[Copyright  Act ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[establish a specific regime for audiovisual
works, protection for which is applicable  in  the case of video games
in other jurisdictions in the absence of a tailored system.  Therefore,
in order to develop a legal regime for creative works in Israel,
including new  types of works like video games, the Israeli
]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act ]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[will
require amendment.]{.stl_10}

[113 ]{.stl_07}[Section 45 of the Israeli ]{.stl_09}[Copyright
Act]{.stl_17 style="font-style:italic;"}[.]{.stl_09}

[page 50]{.stl_10}

[ITALY]{.stl_11}

[137. ]{.stl_12}[To date, there is no specific regulation for or
definition of video games under Italian law.  In Italy, multimedia works
were not expressly defined by the ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act of
1941]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[,  amended in 2003 (hereafter,
the Italian ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[); however, they are mentioned in  Article
171-]{.stl_10}[ter ]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[f
]{.stl_10}[bis ]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[regarding criminal
infringement and Article 181-]{.stl_10}[bis]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[, which provide for  the obligation to affix
an SIAE]{.stl_10}^[114\ ]{.stl_16}^[label to both software and
multimedia works in order to  guarantee their originality. The
construction of the legal status of video games has been  created by
jurisprudence and doctrine.]{.stl_10}

[CLASSIFICATION OF VIDEO GAMES]{.stl_10}

[138. ]{.stl_12}[Video games were defined for the first time in an
Italian jurisdiction as ―]{.stl_15}[gadgets created to  relieve idle
people from boredom]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[‖ (Turin
Magistrate Court, May 25, 1982), the ]{.stl_15}[ classification as
software fell outside of copyright protection at that
time.]{.stl_10}^[115\ ]{.stl_16}^[However,  copying was prevented under
the ]{.stl_10}[Unfair Competition ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[law. A subsequent judgment by the
]{.stl_10}[ Turin Court (―Atari‖ Judgment, October 17, 1983) focused on
the ―images in motion‖ ]{.stl_15}[ element that characterizes any video
game, classifying it as an audiovisual work, thus  opening the door for
copyright protection and its applicable regime regarding
infringement  and illegal copying. The case law alternated between
classifications as software]{.stl_10}^[116\ ]{.stl_16}^[and as  images
in motion when seizing unauthorized copies for
sale,]{.stl_10}^[117\ ]{.stl_16}^[although the copies did  not bear the
SIAE label.]{.stl_10}

[139. ]{.stl_12}[The Italian Supreme Court, aware of the gap in the
legislation and of the fact that the ]{.stl_10}[ concept of ―images in
motion‖ was not sufficient to encompass the complexity of video
]{.stl_15}[ games, finally classified them as multimedia works in the
noteworthy Dalvit Judgment of  May 25,
2007.]{.stl_10}^[118\ ]{.stl_16}^[This legal status has been confirmed
by subsequent case law.]{.stl_10}^[119\ ]{.stl_16}^[It must  be noted,
however, that the rationale for this Judgment was limited to a criminal
approach,  in that the judges, after classifying video games as
multimedia works, consequently  applied criminal sanctions regarding
infringing copies pursuant to Article 171  ]{.stl_10}[ter ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[f ]{.stl_10}[bis ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[of  the Italian ]{.stl_10}[Copyright
Act]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[.]{.stl_10}

[THE DOCTRINE QUALIFICATION]{.stl_10}

[140. ]{.stl_12}[Italian doctrin]{.stl_10}[e has thus created a
definition of the multimedia work: ―]{.stl_15}[a product that  combines
simultaneously, in a digital form, text, graphics, sounds, images
and  software.]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[‖]{.stl_15}^[120\ ]{.stl_16}^[The
distinctive feature of these new media is their interactivity, which
allows  the user ]{.stl_10}[-- ]{.stl_15}[through the use of software
]{.stl_10}[-- ]{.stl_15}[to combine different media by linking them at
the  same time. Therefore, video games seem to fall within this
category, because the player  can interact with the story by repeatedly
choosing the path, the scene, the sounds and the  characters.]{.stl_10}

[Part of the doctrine suggests that, due to their nature, video games
should fall within the]{.stl_10}

[category of collective works (Article 3 of the Italian
]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[), as
collections of]{.stl_10}

[114 ]{.stl_07}[Società Italiana degli Autori ed Editori, which is the
Italian Authors and Publishers collection  society.]{.stl_09}

[115 ]{.stl_07}[Judgment of the Italian  Supreme Court, November 24,
1986,  which expressly recognized copyright  protection]{.stl_09}

[for software on the grounds that  its technical-conventional language
could be analogous to  the alphabet or the seven]{.stl_09}

[musical notes.]{.stl_09}

[116 ]{.stl_07}[Supreme Court, Crim. Div., July 4, 1997.]{.stl_09}

[117 ]{.stl_07}[Supreme Court Crim. Div., December 15, 2006.]{.stl_09}

[118 ]{.stl_07}[This case was related to violation of digital rights
management  (DRMs) where the defendant was charged with]{.stl_09}

[making an infringing chipset.]{.stl_09}

[119 ]{.stl_07}[Supreme Court Judgments, January 14, 2009, and March 4,
2011.]{.stl_09}

[120 ]{.stl_07}[Cunegatti,  ]{.stl_09}[Aspetti legali  dell'opera
multimediale]{.stl_18 style="font-style:italic;"}[, Guerini,  2000;
Guglielmetti,  ]{.stl_09}[Le opere  multimediali]{.stl_17
style="font-style:italic;"}[, AIDA,]{.stl_09}

[1998, 132.]{.stl_09}

[page 51]{.stl_10}

[autonomous works under the supervision of an editor, which are
protected ]{.stl_10}[per se ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[and]{.stl_10}

[independently of the protection of the individual works.]{.stl_10}

[According to another doctrinal trend, emphasis is given to the
audiovisual nature of video games, which could therefore be considered
cinematographic works (implied by the Atari Judgment, 1983), due to the
involvement of a plurality of authors as provided by Article 44 of the
Italian ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[(with respect to script, screenplay and
music, in addition to the director) and the exercise of all economic
rights of exploitation by the producer.]{.stl_10}

[The issue thus remains open for a clear classification of video games.
In general, however, it could be concluded that the case law, in the
absence of a legal definition, has moved from a simplistic approach to
video games as mere software works regulated by Article 64
]{.stl_10}[bis et seq. ]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[of the
Italian ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[(which could only apply to some basic
examples of video games]{.stl_10}^[121]{.stl_16}^[) towards construing
them as multimedia or cinematographic works.]{.stl_10}

[Once the existence of video games has been recognized by the legal
system, the second essential aspect is the determination of the
different authors involved in the creative process.]{.stl_10}

[AUTHORS]{.stl_10}

[141. ]{.stl_12}[Identification of the authors of a video game
necessarily follows from their  legal]{.stl_10}

[classification.]{.stl_10}

[If a video game is construed as a collective work, all authors of a
creative contribution to the video game may be considered authors of
their individual contribution, while the editor would own the copyright
in the video game as a collective work.]{.stl_10}

[If a video game is treated as a cinematographic work, as seems to be
the current trend in Italy, co-ownership could be deemed to exist
between the authors of the script, of the screenplay and of the music,
as well as the director (considered the person coordinating the
different contributions). In light of the particular features of video
games, the graphic designer and the author of the software could also be
considered co-authors of the video game. The issue, however, does not
appear to have been resolved in Italian case law and needs to be
considered on a case-by-case basis.]{.stl_10}

[142. ]{.stl_12}[A new problem that has arisen as the video game
industry has evolved, concerns the  contributions by players involved in
interactive online gaming. In principle, all creative  contributions to
an existing work are protected as autonomous works.
However,  exploitation of the new work requires authorization by the
owner of the rights in the  original work. In the absence of such
authorization, copyright infringement could be  established. However,
this has been disputed in academic legal writing, a stricter view  being
that modification of a digital work ]{.stl_10}[-- ]{.stl_15}[implying
its reproduction ]{.stl_10}[-- ]{.stl_15}[would always  require  the
consent of the rights holder, irrespective of its economic exploitation
and whether or  not the reproduction is made for private use.]{.stl_10}

[The issue should therefore first be addressed by the video game
industry in determining ]{.stl_10}[how far it should embrace players'
contributions ]{.stl_15}[in creating new material, either through
encouraging mod-communities or enclosing video games in heavily policed
copyright regimes.]{.stl_10}

[121 ]{.stl_07}[―]{.stl_08}[Videogiochi  in cerca  di diritto
di  autore]{.stl_17 style="font-style:italic;"}[‖]{.stl_08}[, by  Dario
Reccia, November  14, 2011  (]{.stl_09}[in English:
―]{.stl_08}[Video  games looking for
copyright]{.stl_09}[‖]{.stl_08}[ ).]{.stl_09}

[page 52]{.stl_10}

[STAKEHOLDERS]{.stl_10}

[143. ]{.stl_12}[The main stakeholders involved in the value chain
are:  a. the manufacturers of the hardware (PCs, game consoles,
smartphones and tablets),  that is, the devices on which the game is
played; the manufacturer of the medium on  which the video game is fixed
(e.g., CDs and DVDs) or of software platforms
(virtual  storage);]{.stl_10}

[b. the original developers of the idea and the software; the authors of
the musical  composition and the author of the images/audiovisual work
(designers, artists),  game testers;]{.stl_10}

[c. the engineers in charge of assembling contents of the multimedia
work (so-called]{.stl_10}

[―production tools‖, middleware);]{.stl_15}

[d. the producer investing the money required to implement the idea; e.
the publisher involved in marketing (i.e., catalogues of games) for
retail and online  distribution; and]{.stl_10}

[f. end-user consumers or players (modifiers).]{.stl_10}

[144. ]{.stl_12}[In the chain of rights, in addition to the authors,
publishers and producers mentioned  above, there are the licensees for
derivative works (e.g., movies, comic books and  merchandising),
licensors for previous rights of the content (e.g., sports games,
books  and  movie characters) as well as of the software/hardware
content; online or rental  distributors; online game equity
investors]{.stl_10}^[122\ ]{.stl_16}^[such as broadband providers,
advertisers and  mobile phone operators.]{.stl_10}

[RELATIONSHIP BETWEEN AUTHORS AND DEVELOPMENT STUDIOS]{.stl_10}

[145. ]{.stl_12}[First, authors can be considered employees where they
are hired as part of the in-house]{.stl_10}

[department by development studios/firms/enterprises.]{.stl_10}

[The second fundamental point is the transfer of rights, which applies
only to rights of economic exploitation of the video ]{.stl_10}[game, as
the author's moral rights (including the right ]{.stl_15}[of paternity
and the right to oppose modifications causing damage to his/her honor
and reputation) cannot be transferred.]{.stl_10}

[The general principle is that the transfer of the rights of economic
exploitation in a creative work must be in writing.]{.stl_10}

[146. ]{.stl_12}[If the author is an employee and creates the work while
performing duties contained in the  employment contract, or upon the
instructions of the employer, the rights of economic  exploitation in
those creative works pertain to the employer (Article 12 ]{.stl_10}[bis
]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[of the Italian
]{.stl_10}[ Copyright Act]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[). The
general application of this principle, which could also be extended
to  works made for hire under the same rationale, is however disputed in
case law and legal  writing, as the law expressly provides for this only
with respect to software and industrial  designs created by employees.
For this reason, it is always advisable that the issue be  settled by
the parties in all relevant labor and work-for-hire contracts by
providing for the  contractual transfer of rights to the employer or to
the entity commissioning the work.]{.stl_10}

[147. ]{.stl_12}[If video games are treated as cinematographic works,
the producer is the only person  entitled to exercise the rights of
economic exploitation (Article 45 of the Italian
]{.stl_10}[Copyright  Act]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[). This
implies, unless provided otherwise by the parties, that the producers
also  acquire ownership of the relevant rights through contracts with
the authors. Certain]{.stl_10}

[122 ]{.stl_07}[[More information is available at:
http://www.tuck.dartmouth.edu/digital/assets/images/05_shah.pdf  page
20.]{.stl_09}](http://www.tuck.dartmouth.edu/digital/assets/images/05_shah.pdf){target="_blank"}

[page 53]{.stl_10}

[opinions in case law and academic legal writing, however, are in favor
of the automatic ownership of those rights by the producer, as implied
by the above rule.]{.stl_10}

[148. ]{.stl_12}[Insofar as a video game is considered a simple
collective work, the publisher that  organizes and coordinates the
different contributions is the owner of the work as  a
whole,  independent of the ownership of each author with respect to
his/her contribution (Article 7  of the Italian ]{.stl_10}[Copyright
Act]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[ ).]{.stl_10}

[149. ]{.stl_12}[Finally, the form of financial compensation available
to the authors, whether as a lump  sum or royalties on the proceeds,
]{.stl_10}[is left to the parties' freedom of
contract]{.stl_15}[.]{.stl_10}

[Specific rules have been laid down with respect to cinematographic
works and could therefore apply to video games, giving authors certain
rights to an additional equitable remuneration, which cannot be waived,
for the case of rental and for each separate use of the work by third
parties which may have not acquired ownership of the relevant rights
(e.g., licensees). The rules applicable to cinematographic works
establish a specific system of remuneration.]{.stl_10}

[Article 46. ]{.stl_10}[bis ]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[of the
Italian ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[provides that, in the case of a transfer of
distribution rights to the producer, authors of audiovisual works and
assimilated works have the right to fair compensation to be paid by
broadcasters for each use of these works by any means of communication
to the public, either by air, cable or satellite. This Article also
provides that for every use of cinematographic or assimilated works
different from that provided in paragraph 1 and Article
18]{.stl_10}[bis]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[, paragraph 5, the
authors of the works themselves are entitled to fair compensation
payable by those exercising the exploitation rights for each separate
commercial use.]{.stl_10}^[123]{.stl_16}^

[POSSIBLE SOLUTIONS]{.stl_10}

[150. ]{.stl_12}[There is a legislative void with regard to the status
of video games in Italy,  and not all  traditional norms created for
particular categories of collaborative works (i.e.,  cinematographic or
collective works) can be applied to them by analogy.]{.stl_10}

[151. ]{.stl_12}[For this reason, possible solutions could include:  a.
creation of an applicable law ]{.stl_10}[sui generis ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[for video games; or  b. adaptation of the
law governing cinematographic works.]{.stl_10}

[152. ]{.stl_12}[In the opinion of some Italian experts, legislators
should propose a specific ]{.stl_10}[sui generis ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[ legal framework for video games. Indeed,
Italy is one of the major consumers of video  games in the EU and,
although it only has four or five national video game
development  studios, the market is growing steadily. According to these
experts, legislators should  propose adequate protection for all people
involved in the creation of video games.]{.stl_10}

[JAPAN]{.stl_11}

[153. ]{.stl_12}[Japan protects created works through the
]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act ]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[(Act No.
48 of May 6, 1970)  (hereafter, the Japanese ]{.stl_10}[Copyright
Act]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[), which protects authors and
performers while  guaranteeing the fair exploitation of these cultural
products and the development
of  culture.]{.stl_10}^[124\ ]{.stl_16}^[However, as in many other
jurisdictions, Article 10 of the Japanese ]{.stl_10}[Copyright  Act
]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[does not specifically define or
refer to video games, although their protection under]{.stl_10}

[123 ]{.stl_07}[Proroga dei termini per la  protezione delle opere
dell'ingegno e dei prodotti  tutelati dalla legge ]{.stl_18
style="font-style:italic;"}[22 aprile 1941.]{.stl_09}

[N 633.]{.stl_09}

[124 ]{.stl_07}[An English translation  of the  Japanese
]{.stl_09}[Copyright Act]{.stl_17 style="font-style:italic;"}[,  by
Yukifusa  Oyama ]{.stl_09}[et al.]{.stl_17
style="font-style:italic;"}[,  Copyright Research  and]{.stl_09}

[[Information Center (CRIC), can be found at:
http://www.cric.or.jp/cric_e/clj/cl2_1.html#cl2_1+SS4]{.stl_09}](http://www.cric.or.jp/cric_e/clj/cl2_1.html#cl2_1+SS4){target="_blank"}

[page 54]{.stl_10}

[the Japanese ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[is unquestioned, because the list of works
in Article 10 is not exhaustive. In this sense, Japanese law in this
area has been derived from judicial precedent beginning in the
1980s.]{.stl_10}

[CLASSIFICATION OF VIDEO GAMES]{.stl_10}

[154. ]{.stl_12}[In the absence of a direct reference to video games in
statutory law, case law has ]{.stl_10}[ recognized video games as
―cinematographic works‖ in accordance with Article 2(3) of the
]{.stl_15}[ Japanese ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[, which includes works ―]{.stl_15}[expressed
by a process producing visual  or audio-visual effects analogous to
those of cinematography and fixed in some material ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[ form.‖]{.stl_19
style="font-style:italic;"}^[125]{.stl_16}^

[155. ]{.stl_12}[The varied judgments of lower courts were harmonized by
the Supreme Court in 2002  (Supreme Court Case No. H13-ju-952) when the
Court affirmed that video games should  be classified as cinematographic
works. ]{.stl_10}[The court's ruling specified that the video game
]{.stl_15}[ in dispute was expressed through a process producing visual
or audiovisual effects similar  to those of cinematography, and
furthermore that such expression was fixed in an object  and thus
rightly classified as a cinematographic work in accordance with Article
2(3) of the  Japanese ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[.]{.stl_10}

[However, not all video games qualify as cinematographic works under the
Japanese ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[.
]{.stl_10}[For example, a game's audiovisual effects might not be
cons]{.stl_15}[idered sufficiently similar to those of traditional
cinematography if its game screens are still images as opposed to
animation.]{.stl_10}^[126]{.stl_16}^

[156. ]{.stl_12}[Despite this limited application of video games as
cinematographic works, protection for  games varies from treatment of
traditional cinematographic works in certain aspects. For  example,
while distribution rights associated with traditional cinematographic
works may  not exhaust under the first-sale doctrine, the Supreme Court
has ruled that such rights for  video games may be exhausted.]{.stl_10}

[Additionally, the computer code used to execute the audiovisual
elements of a given video game can be also protected under the Japanese
]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act ]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[as a
literary work. Nonetheless, Article 10 specifies that such protection
does not cover the programming language, the rules and algorithms of a
computer program, and that only the source code shall enjoy protection,
provided it is creative and original.]{.stl_10}

[157. ]{.stl_12}[Therefore, video games can have a distributive
qualification in Japan, although before  determining whether a
particular video game can be protected as both a computer  program and a
cinematographic work, an analysis must be performed in order
to  determine the specific characteristics of the work.]{.stl_10}

[RIGHTS HOLDERS AND STAKEHOLDERS]{.stl_10}

[158. ]{.stl_12}[As with traditional cinematographic works, the
determination of authorship is the key to  establishing ownership of
video games. As set forth in the Japanese ]{.stl_10}[Copyright
Act]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[,  creators, producers or
publishers may all be considered authors:]{.stl_10}

[i. Creators are presumptive authors: A person whose name or appellation
(hereinafter ]{.stl_10}[ referred to as ―true name‖), or whose generally
known pen name, abbreviation or ]{.stl_15}[ other substitute for his or
her true name is indicated as the name of the author in the]{.stl_10}

[125 ]{.stl_07}[Tokyo  District  Court  Case  No. S56-wa-8371;
1984/9/28; Tokyo  District  Court  Case  No. H4-wa-19495;]{.stl_09}

[1994/1/31; Osaka High Court Case No. H9-ne-3587; 1999/4/27; Supreme
Court Case No. H13-ju-952; 2002/4/25. ]{.stl_09}[126 ]{.stl_07}[Tokyo
High Court Case No. H7-ne-3344.]{.stl_09}

[page 55]{.stl_10}

[customary manner on the original of the work or where the work is
offered to or made available to the public, shall be presumed to be the
author of that work;]{.stl_10}^[127]{.stl_16}^

[ii. Creative contribution by producer: Where one or more producers
contribute to the  creation of the work as a whole, the producers are
qualified as authors. The  authorship of a cinematographic work shall be
attributed to those who, by taking  charge of, for example, producing,
directing, filming or art direction, have contributed  to the creation
of that work as a whole, excluding authors of novels, scenarios,  music
or other works adapted or reproduced in that
work;]{.stl_10}^[128]{.stl_16}^

[iii. Authorship of a work made by an employee in the course of his or
her duties:  However, authorship can be attributed to a publisher (legal
person) where the work  is made by its employee(s) on the initiative of
the publisher.]{.stl_10}^[129]{.stl_16}^

[The employee may maintain independent authorship rights:]{.stl_10}

[a. if the work is not created on the initiative of the employer; b.
]{.stl_10}[if the work is not created in the course of the employee's
duties; ]{.stl_15}[c. if the work is not made public under the name of
the employer; or d. if the employment contract stipulates specifically
that the employer will not ]{.stl_10}[ be an author of the employee's
creation.]{.stl_15}

[Therefore, in the case of a video game created by an employee in the
course of his or her duties, the copyright shall be originally
attributed to the publisher with no transfer of rights from the creator.
Any other transfer of rights from the authors would require a written or
verbal contract and could be made in whole or in part.]{.stl_10}

[REMUNERATION]{.stl_10}

[159. ]{.stl_12}[For employees whose creative contributions are made
during the course of their duties,  because there is no transfer of
copyright from employee to employer, no additional  compensation other
than salary is required. In all other cases, the original
contributor  would be considered a creator/publisher and would be
compensated according to the  terms and conditions of the contract,
which may include a lump sum or proportional  compensation, depending on
the agreement reached by the parties.]{.stl_10}

[160. ]{.stl_12}[The Japanese ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[includes a system for exploiting works under
compulsory  license, specifically for those works whose rights holders
cannot be found because they  are unknown or for similar such
reasons.]{.stl_10}^[130\ ]{.stl_16}^[Video game enthusiasts have coined
the term ]{.stl_10}[ ―]{.stl_15}[abandonware ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[video game‖ ]{.stl_19
style="font-style:italic;"}[for older games for which copyrights are
unclear for various  reasons and that are no longer available for
purchase. In legal terms, they would be ]{.stl_10}[ ―]{.stl_15}[orphan
works‖]{.stl_19 style="font-style:italic;"}[. Therefore, under Japanese
law, any person willing to exploit a particular  video game may require
a license from the Commissioner of the Agency for Cultural  Affairs,
provided that the following requirements are fulfilled:]{.stl_10}

[a. The video game was made public or made available to the public for
a  considerable period of time;]{.stl_10}

[b. After due diligence, the copyright owner cannot be found; and c. The
solicitor shall deposit, on behalf of the copyright owner,
compensation  fixed by the Commissioner.]{.stl_10}

[127 ]{.stl_07}[Article 14 of the Japanese ]{.stl_09}[Copyright
Act]{.stl_17 style="font-style:italic;"}[. ]{.stl_09}[128
]{.stl_07}[Article 16 of the Japanese ]{.stl_09}[Copyright Act]{.stl_17
style="font-style:italic;"}[. ]{.stl_09}[129 ]{.stl_07}[Article 15 of
the Japanese ]{.stl_09}[Copyright Act]{.stl_17
style="font-style:italic;"}[. ]{.stl_09}[130 ]{.stl_07}[Article 67 of
the Japanese ]{.stl_09}[Copyright Act]{.stl_17
style="font-style:italic;"}[.]{.stl_09}

[page 56]{.stl_10}

[161. ]{.stl_12}[Therefore, according to the Japanese Supreme Court,
video games can qualify as  cinematographic works where they produce
visual and audiovisual effects similar to those  of movies and other
audiovisual works, although this might simply be an attempt
to  accommodate these modern works within an existing category. A new
legal regime is  needed in Japan that is more suitable to video games
and that takes into account their  specific elements (e.g.,
interactivity, complexity and the number of potential
authors  involved).]{.stl_10}

[KENYA]{.stl_11}

[162. ]{.stl_12}[The ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[, Chapter 130 of February 1, 2003, and the
]{.stl_10}[Copyright Regulations of  2004 ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[are the main regulations governing copyright
in Kenya (hereinafter, collectively the  Kenyan ]{.stl_10}[Copyright
Act]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[). Indeed, the Kenyan
]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[establishes that ―artistic work‖
]{.stl_15}[ means, irrespective of artistic quality, any of the
following or works similar thereto:  paintings, drawings, etchings,
lithographs, woodcuts, engravings, prints;  maps, plans and  diagrams;
works of sculpture; photographs not comprised in audiovisual works;
works  of  architecture in the form of buildings or models and works of
artistic craftsmanship, pictorial  woven tissues and articles of applied
handicraft and industrial art.]{.stl_10}^[131]{.stl_16}^

[The preliminary section also contains a specif]{.stl_10}[ic definition
of ―]{.stl_15}[audio-visual works]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[‖
which, in ]{.stl_15}[the opinion of some experts, could include video
games, as there is no specific mention of this kind of work in the
Kenyan ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[.]{.stl_10}

[CLASSIFICATION OF VIDEO GAMES]{.stl_10}

[163. ]{.stl_12}[The Kenyan ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[defines aud]{.stl_10}[iovisual works as
―]{.stl_15}[a fixation in any physical  medium of images, either
synchronized with or without sound, from which a moving  picture may by
any means be reproduced and includes videotapes and video games but
]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[ doesn't include a
broadcast.]{.stl_19
style="font-style:italic;"}[‖]{.stl_15}^[132\ ]{.stl_16}^[This is a
statutory definition derived from the Kenyan ]{.stl_10}[ Copyright
Act]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[, but there is no case law that
completes this legal definition with respect to  video games.]{.stl_10}

[According to this definition, the protection given to audiovisual works
would also be applicable to video games. In this regard, Section 22 of
the Kenyan ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[establishes the works eligible for
copyright, including what appears to be an exhaustive list of items:
literary works, musical works, artistic works, audiovisual works, sound
recordings and broadcasts.]{.stl_10}^[133\ ]{.stl_16}^[As there is no
specific mention of video games, they must be classified in one or more
of these categories, i.e., as artistic or audiovisual works.]{.stl_10}

[164. ]{.stl_12}[The specific protection for audiovisual works is
defined in Section 26 of the Kenyan ]{.stl_10}[ Copyright Act]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[, which establishes a list of acts protected
by the law and others expressly  excluded from such protection,
constituting the exceptions of exclusive
rights.]{.stl_10}^[134]{.stl_16}^

[In general terms, video games can be qualified as
]{.stl_10}[audiovisual works ]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[based
on the Kenyan ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[. However, given the complex nature of this
type of work of authorship, other creative elements can be found,
including characters, graphics and computer code; all of them enjoying
protection under the Kenyan ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[. Regarding the computer program underlying
a given video game, the Kenyan ]{.stl_10}[Copyright]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}

[131 ]{.stl_07}[Preliminary 2(1) of the Kenyan ]{.stl_09}[Copyright
Act.]{.stl_17 style="font-style:italic;"}

[132 ]{.stl_07}[Preliminary (2) of the Kenyan ]{.stl_09}[Copyright
Act]{.stl_17 style="font-style:italic;"}[.]{.stl_09}

[133 ]{.stl_07}[Part III Copyright and Other Related Rights, Section
22(1) of the Kenyan ]{.stl_09}[Copyright Act]{.stl_17
style="font-style:italic;"}[. ]{.stl_09}[134 ]{.stl_07}[Section 26 (1)
of the Kenyan ]{.stl_09}[Copyright Act.]{.stl_17
style="font-style:italic;"}

[page 57]{.stl_10}

[Act ]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[defines it as ―]{.stl_15}[a
set of instructions expressed in words, codes, schemes or in any other
form, which is capable, when incorporated in a medium that the computer
can read, of causing a com]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[puter to
perform or achieve a particular task or result.‖ ]{.stl_19
style="font-style:italic;"}[The computer program embedded in a video
game falls, without any doubt, within this definition.]{.stl_10}

[Therefore, Kenya compares video games with audiovisual works, providing
to video games the same legal protection as to films or movies.
Nonetheless, other elements of video games, like the computer code, can
enjoy independent protection, although covering only the protected work
(that is, the software) itself.]{.stl_10}

[RIGHTS HOLDERS AND STAKEHOLDERS]{.stl_10}

[165. ]{.stl_12}[Protecti]{.stl_10}[on of authors' rights differs in
Kenya depending on the created work]{.stl_15}[. Thus,  according to the
Kenyan ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[,
the ]{.stl_10}[author ]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[of a
literary, musical or artistic work is  the person who first makes or
creates the work. However, the ]{.stl_10}[author ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[of an audiovisual  work is the person who
made the arrangements for the making of the
work.]{.stl_10}^[135\ ]{.stl_16}^[Therefore,  authors of a script,
characters or creative content will retain such status, while
the  contributors to an audiovisual work (e.g., a video game) will not
retain such rights in favor  of the studio or producer which arranged
all the elements to create the work.]{.stl_10}

[166. ]{.stl_12}[Although the copyright vests automatically with the
initial author,]{.stl_10}^[136\ ]{.stl_16}^[where a literary,
]{.stl_10}[ musical or artistic work is commissioned by a person who is
not the author's employer ]{.stl_15}[ under a contract of
service]{.stl_10}^[137\ ]{.stl_16}^[or, not having been so commissioned,
is made in the course ]{.stl_10}[ of the author's employment under a
contract of service,]{.stl_15}^[138\ ]{.stl_16}^[the copyright shall be
deemed ]{.stl_10}[ to be transferred to the person who commissioned the
work or the author's employer, ]{.stl_15}[ subject to any agreement
between the parties excluding or limiting the
transfer.]{.stl_10}^[139  ]{.stl_16}^[In this  case, the author shall
retain the moral rights, but the patrimonial rights are
deemed  transferred to the commissioner.]{.stl_10}

[Therefore, under the Kenyan ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[, the rights regime is quite complex and
confusing, because original creators of a literary, musical or artistic
work will be the ]{.stl_10}[authors ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[of the work, maintaining all copyrights in
the work (unless it was commissioned or where an employment contract
exists). However, if the work has an audiovisual character, the original
contributors will not be the ]{.stl_10}[authors ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[but the person making the arrangements for
the making of the film will be the author. As a result, with regard to
video games it is essential to ascertain the legal nature and
classification of this type of work in order to determine the applicable
rights regime.]{.stl_10}

[167. ]{.stl_12}[However, video games can be created by one or more
authors; where this is the case, ]{.stl_10}[ joint authorship can exist,
which is defined by the law ―]{.stl_15}[as a work produced by
the  collaboration of two or more authors in which the contribution of
each author is not  separable from the contribution of the other author
or authors]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[.‖ In this case, the
copyrights ]{.stl_15}[ in the work shall vest jointly in the co-authors,
who must authorize any exploitation of the  work.]{.stl_10}

[168. ]{.stl_12}[Video game rights are transmissible by assignment, by
license, testamentary disposition]{.stl_10}

[or by operation of law as movable
property.]{.stl_10}^[140\ ]{.stl_16}^[An assignment or testamentary
disposition]{.stl_10}

by the parties. In any case, the Kenyan ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act
]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[makes no mention of  the
compensation that authors (whether employees or independent contractors)
shall  receive; therefore, any remuneration or royalty scheme must be
contractually established  between the contributor and the assignee of a
given video game.]{.stl_10}

[FOLKLORE AND THE PUBLIC DOMAIN]{.stl_10}

[171. ]{.stl_12}[Finally, the Kenyan ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[establishes a specific legal framework for
folklore as  part of the national culture and heritage. Therefore, if a
video game author or studio  includes any work of Kenyan folklore in a
given video game, they will have to respect  Section 49 of the Kenyan
]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[.]{.stl_10}

[The specific definition of folklore is a literary, musical or artistic
work presumed to have been created within Kenya by an unidentified
author, and which has been passed on from one generation to another and
constitutes a basic element of the traditional cultural heritage of
Kenya. Such works include: folktales, folk poetry and folk riddles; folk
songs and instrumental folk music; folk dances and folk plays; and the
production of folk art, in particular drawings, paintings, sculptures,
pottery, woodwork, metalware
and  jewelry.]{.stl_10}^[145\ ]{.stl_16}^[Considering its national
interest, the Government of Kenya may issue further implementing
regulations with respect to copyright protection of folklore, including
the authorization and prescription of the terms and conditions governing
any specified use of folklore, except by a national public entity for
non-commercial purposes, on the importation of any work made abroad that
embodies folklore.]{.stl_10}^[146]{.stl_16}^

[172. ]{.stl_12}[In conclusion, Kenya has legislation that protects
authors and the creation of original  works of au]{.stl_10}[thorship,
although video games do not easily fit within Kenya's current  legal
]{.stl_15}[ framework. Moreover, no video game case has so far been
decided by the Kenyan  courts. An amendment to the Kenyan
]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act ]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[is
therefore needed to clarify the  unresolved issues described
above.]{.stl_10}

[REPUBLIC OF KOREA]{.stl_11}

[CLASSIFICATION OF VIDEO GAMES]{.stl_10}

[173. ]{.stl_12}[Although the Republic of Korea has a highly developed
video game industry, there are no  provisions in the relevant Republic
of Korea laws that define or classify ]{.stl_10}[video games]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[.  However, video games are undisputedly
considered to qualify as computer programs,  and  they have been
proteced as such from the time of earliest production. Computer
programs  are protected in the Republic of Korea through the
]{.stl_10}[Computer Programs Protection Act ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[of ]{.stl_10}[ 1986, which embodies
―]{.stl_15}[creative works expressed as a series of instructions
and  commands used directly or indirectly in an apparatus having data
processing capacity  such as a computer, etc. ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[(hereinafter referred to as ―computer‖) for
the purpose of ]{.stl_19 style="font-style:italic;"}[ obtaining a
certain result]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[.‖]{.stl_15}^[147]{.stl_16}^

[As the video game industry has been developing rapidly in recent years
in the Republic of Korea, there has been much discussion about effective
means for protecting video games. As a result, jurisprudence and
doctrine have begun to recognize video games as audiovisual or
cinematographic works in cases where they satisfy the prerequisites
established in the Republic of Korea ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[of 2009 (hereinafter, the Republic of Korea
]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[ ).]{.stl_10}

[The Republic of Korea ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[, Article 2 (13), defines a ―cinematographic
work‖ as ―]{.stl_15}[the creative production in which a series of images
(regardless of whether or not accompanied by sound) are collected, and
which can be played by mechanical or electronic devices and can be seen,
or both seen and heard]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[.‖ In this
regard, secondary ]{.stl_15}[protection of cinematographic works by
trademarks and publicity rights of professional gamers has also recently
come under discussion.]{.stl_10}

[In the case of a video game that falls within the definitions of both
computer programs  and cinematographic works, the author or owner of a
video game generally seeks to protect it as a cinematographic work under
the Republic of Korea ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[, as they are afforded much stronger
protection.]{.stl_10}

[174. ]{.stl_12}[Finally, some theories suggest that video games qualify
as ―collective works‖, although]{.stl_15}

[there is no provision that specifically defines a ―collective work‖
under Republic of Korea]{.stl_15}

[law.]{.stl_10}

[AUTHOR-RELATED ISSUES REGARDING VIDEO GAMES]{.stl_10}

[175. ]{.stl_12}[In the case of video games that qualify as
cinematographic works, ―]{.stl_15}[a
corporation  or  organization]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[‖,
that is, game producers, are presumed to be the ]{.stl_15}[author
]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[where a labor  relationship
exists.]{.stl_10}^[148\ ]{.stl_16}^[This is because numerous people are
involved in the production of  cinematographic works, making it very
complicated and difficult to determine authorship, in  addition to
giving rise to many problems with regard to exploitation rights.
However, where  employees of video game studios have virtually created
video games or contributed  significantly to the creation of such video
games,]{.stl_10}^[149\ ]{.stl_16}^[and in the case where the
―employee]{.stl_15}

[147 ]{.stl_07}[Computer Programs Protection Act]{.stl_17
style="font-style:italic;"}[, Act No. 3920. December 31, 1986, last
amended by Act No. 5605.]{.stl_09}

[December 30, 1998.]{.stl_09}

[His Duties)]{.stl_17 style="font-style:italic;"}[: ―]{.stl_18
style="font-style:italic;"}[The authorship of a work which is made by an
employee of a legal person, etc. during the course of his duties and is
made public under the name of such a legal person, etc. as the author
shall be attributed to that legal person, etc., unless otherwise

[requirement for computer program works.]{.stl_17

[rules of the company‖ provide for the recognition of the person who

employee may qualify as the author. The same principle applies,
]{.stl_10}[mutatis mutandis]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[, to
computer programs, as per Article 7 of the ]{.stl_10}[Computer Programs
Protection Act]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[.]{.stl_10}

[176. ]{.stl_12}[In the case where there is no employee rule recognizing
employees as authors, the  Republic of Korea ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act
]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[provides ―Chapter ]{.stl_15}[V
Special Cases Concerning ]{.stl_10}[ Cinematographic Works‖ in order to
clarify the relationship of the rights and duties in
]{.stl_15}[ relation to cinematographic works and to encourage the
active use of these works. Under  Article 100 of the Republic of Korea
]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[, where a
producer of a cinematographic  work and a person who agree to cooperate
in producing such a work have obtained a  copyright in the said work,
the rights necessary for the exploitation of the work shall,  unless
there exists a special agreement to the contrary, be presumed to have
been  transferred to the producer of the cinematographic work. However,
the copyright of the  authors or owners in the orignal works (e.g., the
novel, play or musical work) for the  production of the cinematographic
work shall not be affected by the said provision.]{.stl_10}

[LEGAL STATUS OF PROFESSIONAL GAMERS]{.stl_10}

[177. ]{.stl_12}[The status of video game players has never been the
subject of a dispute in the Republic  of Korea; nonetheless,
jurisprudence and scholars concur that video games played by  players
are not recognized as copyrightable works ]{.stl_10}[per se]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[. According to some theories,  players may
qualify as performers. However, their share in the copyright in the
works has  not, as yet, been recognized, and there has been no reported
legal dispute concerning  their performance.]{.stl_10}

[The cash prizes awarded by video game companies or organizers of video
game competitions are the main source of income for players. However,
star players who become professionals enjoy press attention and
popularity equal to that of other celebrities in the Republic of Korea,
and they can earn additional income, for example, by appearing in
advertisements. ]{.stl_10}[In this case, players' publicity rights can
be the subject of disputes ]{.stl_15}[against contest organizers and
video game producers.]{.stl_10}

[STAKEHOLDERS IN THE VALUE CHAIN OF VIDEO GAMES]{.stl_10}

[178. ]{.stl_12}[Considering the growth and development of the Republic
of Korea video game sector,  many stakeholders have emerged, not only
those involved directly in the production and  commercialization of
video games, but also other persons, such as contest
organizers,  professional gamers and television networks that broadcast
such events. This scenario  implies that the Republic of Korea is one of
the most regulated countries in this regard,  including the
establishment of a public entity with oversight responsibility for video
games  and the companies involved in this
sector.]{.stl_10}^[150]{.stl_16}^

[Therefore, the main stakeholders involved in this sector in the
Republic of Korea are:]{.stl_10}

[a. The producer of a video game is the most important stakeholder in
the value chain  where a video game falls under the definition of a
cinematographic work, because  the producer is properly entitled to its
exploitation;]{.stl_10}

[150 ]{.stl_07}[This entity is the ―Game Rating Board‖ (GRB),
established in 2006 under the ]{.stl_08}[Game Industry Promotion Act
]{.stl_17 style="font-style:italic;"}[as]{.stl_09}

[[a public organization for fostering the sound game culture and
developing the game industry in  the Republic of Korea. The GRB is
independently administered for the classification of game contents
manufactured  and distributed in the Republic of Korea. The Rating Board
also reviews illegally distributed game websites, arcade game machines
and gambling games in order to protect the public from such negative
influences as illegal gambling,  excessive violence and nudity. More
information is available at:
http://www.grb.or.kr/english/about/overview.aspx.]{.stl_09}](http://www.grb.or.kr/english/about/overview.aspx){target="_blank"}

[page 61]{.stl_10}

[b. The authors/owners of the original copyrighted works, such as a
novel or play,  used in creating the video game;]{.stl_10}

[c. Every participant who has made a creative contribution to the
completion of the  video game as a cinematographic work, such as
editors, graphic designers, game  testers and software
engineers;]{.stl_10}

[d. The broadcasting companies with the equipment to broadcast popular
video games  played publicly by professional gamers (players);]{.stl_10}

[e. Organizers of popular video game competitions;]{.stl_10}

[f. Professional gamers (the professional players of famous video
games).]{.stl_10}

[EMPLOYEE-RELATED ISSUSES IN THE CREATION OF VIDEO GAMES]{.stl_10}

[179. ]{.stl_12}[As described above, the Republic of Korea has
determined that, in an employer-employee  relationship, and in the
absence of a written agreement, the copyrights in the work shall  vest
with the company, as shall the qualification as the
]{.stl_10}[author]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[. Furthermore, if
the author  is an employee, he or she may be compensated in any way that
is determined by the  employee rules or agreement, regardless of the
fact that he or she is entitled to be known  as the author of the video
game.]{.stl_10}

[However, where a video game is produced by independent contractors,
compensation may be awarded according to the terms and conditions agreed
upon by the parties. In all cases, should the compensation awarded to
the author be so unsubstantial as to be unfair even though the amount of
the remuneration was paid according to the agreement, the courts can
waive the agreements or employee rules and order compensation in a
reasonable amount.]{.stl_10}

[TRANSFER OF RIGHTS]{.stl_10}

[180. ]{.stl_12}[In the case of video games that qualify as
cinematographic works, the author, having  produced the game, is
presumed to have the rights to broadcast, publicly present,  transmit,
reproduce, distribute and create derivative works
thereof.]{.stl_10}^[151\ ]{.stl_16}^[This stipulation  is  particularly
important in a country like the Republic of Korea, where there exists
a  secondary market for the exploitation of video games (e.g., in
competitions and  merchandising). If a person who has an agreement with
a producer of a cinematographic  work regarding cooperation in the
production of such a work has obtained the copyright  in  the work, it
is presumed that the rights necessary for the use of the work are
transferred to  the producer, unless provided otherwise under the
Republic of Korea ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[,  Article 100.]{.stl_10}

[However, in the case in which the person who consents to cooperate in
the production of a cinematographic work agrees to transfer his or her
copyright to the video game producer, such agreement takes precedence
over the above presumptive provisons of the Republic of Korea
]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[.]{.stl_10}

[151 ]{.stl_07}[Article 99 of the Republic of Korea ]{.stl_09}[Copyright
Act]{.stl_17 style="font-style:italic;"}[.]{.stl_09}

[page 62]{.stl_10}

[RIGHT TO BROADCAST GAMES PLAYED BY PROFESSIONAL GAMERS]{.stl_10}

[181. ]{.stl_12}[With regard to video games, the most contentious issues
in Republic of Korea courts have  been whether the video games at issue
involve sufficient creativity to be protected  as  copyrighted works.
Thus, video games that qualify as cinematographic works in the  Republic
of Korea enjoy as much copyright protection as they would in any other
country.  In the case of video games that do not satisfy the standards
of cinematographic works,  these works enjoy protection as computer
programs.]{.stl_10}

[182. ]{.stl_12}[The growing popularity of video games has led to the
live broadcasting of video game  competitions on sports or game channels
and, in return, such activities have contributed to ]{.stl_10}[ further
developments in the video game industry and the games' increasing
popularity]{.stl_15}[. At  the same time, this growing popularity has
entailed, as a result of the live broadcasting of  video game
competitions, disputes between game producers, i.e., the copyright
owners  of  video games, and broadcasters, over the performance and
broadcasting rights in the video  games played by the players.]{.stl_10}

[Video game producers are fully protected under the Republic of Korea
]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act ]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[as
authors of video games, i.e., cinematographic works. In contrast,
broadcasters bear the burden of justifying allegations of infringement
through specific reasoning, such as: (i) counter-]{.stl_10}[statements
based on a ―quotation from works made public‖, allowed ]{.stl_15}[under
the Republic of Korea ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[; (ii) the principle of fair use; and (iii)
counter-statements grounded in other laws (e.g., freedom of expression
or the rule of good faith).]{.stl_10}

[With respect to the ―principle of fair use‖, this has not been, until
]{.stl_15}[recently, included  as a general clause in the Republic of
Korea ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[.
Thus, the jurisprudence was reluctant to recognize instances of fair use
that were not among those specifically set out and limited in number in
the Republic of Korea ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[. However, as a result of the
]{.stl_10}[incorporation of ―U.S.]{.stl_15}[-]{.stl_10}[Korea Free Trade
Agreement‖ clauses into Republic of Korea laws, ]{.stl_15}[the principle
of fair use is now included as a general clause in the amended Republic
of Korea ]{.stl_10}[Copyright Act]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[.]{.stl_10}^[152\ ]{.stl_16}^[Accordingly,
when copyright infringement disputes over performance or broadcasting
rights in video game competitions arise between the author of a
cinematographic work and a broadcaster, such disputes may be resolved
pursuant to the newly-added provision on fair use.]{.stl_10}

[183. ]{.stl_12}[Therefore, the Republic of Korea probably has the most
developed video game industry in  the world, including professional
gamers and parallel industries that generate important  revenue from
video games. However, the legal classification of video games is not
entirely  settled, as it is not clear whether video games have a
distributive classification or are  compounded by a single object. These
issues will require clarification in the future,  particularly with
regard to the legal status of the video and images that result from
a  specific execution of a video game.]{.stl_10}

[RUSSIAN FEDERATION]{.stl_11}

]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[(hereinafter, the Russian

[CLASSIFICATION OF VIDEO GAMES]{.stl_10}

[185. ]{.stl_12}[Article 1.225 of the Russian Federation
]{.stl_10}[Civil Code ]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[establishes
that the results of  intellectual activity and means equated to them of
individualization of legal entities, goods,  work, services and
enterprises that are granted legal protection (intellectual
property)  include: works of science, literature and
art,]{.stl_10}^[154\ ]{.stl_16}^[and computer
programs.]{.stl_10}^[155\ ]{.stl_16}^[Article 1.259 ]{.stl_10}[ defines
the objects of copyright as ―]{.stl_15}[works of science, literature and
art, regardless  of the  value and purpose of the works as well as the
mode of their expression]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[‖,
including, in a ]{.stl_15}[ non-exhaustive list, literary works,
audiovisual works and computer programs, which are  protected as
literary works. Nonetheless, Russian law does not specifically define
video  games as being a particular kind of intellectual property, and
therefore we shall analyze  their classification in other systems, for
example as computer programs or  audiovisual  works.]{.stl_10}

[186. ]{.stl_12}[It is also noteworthy with regard to video
]{.stl_10}[game protection that: ―]{.stl_15}[copyright extends to
part  of a work, to its name, and to a character in the work if by its
nature it can be recognized  as an independent result of the creative
work of the author and it satisfies the  requirements established by
paragraph 3]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[‖]{.stl_15}^[156\ ]{.stl_16}^[of the same
Article. Therefore, individual  elements of video games, such as the
characters, set-ups and graphics, may also be  eligible for copyright
protection, provided they are creative and original.]{.stl_10}

[Judicial practice is also not widely developed in this
area.]{.stl_10}^[157\ ]{.stl_16}^[However, there have been some cases in
which the legal nature of video games was analyzed for the purpose of
legal protection against counterfeiting.]{.stl_10}

[187. ]{.stl_12}[Generally, video games should be considered software,
which is copyrightable under  Russian law. The Russian Federation
]{.stl_10}[Civil Code ]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[also
considers that computer programs  are copyrightable and protected as
literary works]{.stl_10}^[158\ ]{.stl_16}^[and that, according to
Russian law,  copyright in all types of computer programs (including
operating systems and program  combinations), which may be expressed in
any language and in any form, including  source code and object code,
shall be protected in the same way as copyright in
literary  works.]{.stl_10}^[159]{.stl_16}^

[However, a video game is a so-]{.stl_10}[called ―complex‖ copyright
object which  ]{.stl_15}[includes different kinds of
copyright-protectable items, such as software, audio elements and
images. Complex works are defined as copyrighted objects containing
several protected elements that result from intellectual activity, such
as cinematographic works, other audiovisual works, theatrical audience
presentations and multimedia products.]{.stl_10}^[160\ ]{.stl_16}^[This
description]{.stl_10}

[154 ]{.stl_07}[The Russian Federation ]{.stl_09}[Civil Code]{.stl_17
style="font-style:italic;"}[.]{.stl_09}

]{.stl_09}[Civil Code]{.stl_17 style="font-style:italic;"}[.]{.stl_09}

[AUTHORS]{.stl_10}

[188. ]{.stl_12}[The legal definition of an author of a work of science,
literature or art is the person by  whose creative labor the work was
made; in this sense, the person indicated as the author  on the original
or other copy of a work shall be considered its author, unless
provided  otherwise.]{.stl_10}^[161]{.stl_16}^

[The Russian Federation ]{.stl_10}[Civil Code ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[considers that the exclusive right to a
result of intellectual activity shall belong to one person or to several
persons jointly. Where the exclusive right to the result of intellectual
activity belongs jointly to several persons, each rights holder shall
have the right to exploit the work at his or her discretion, unless the
Russian Federation ]{.stl_10}[Civil Code]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[, or an agreement between the rights
holders, provides otherwise. The relationship of the persons jointly
possessing the exclusive right shall be determined by agreement among
the parties. The income from the joint use of the result of intellectual
activity shall be shared equally among all rights holders, unless they
have agreed otherwise in writing. The use of the exclusive right to the
result of intellectual activity or to means of individualization shall
be determined jointly by the rights holders, unless otherwise provided
for in the Russian Federation ]{.stl_10}[Civil Code.]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}^[162]{.stl_16}^

[189. ]{.stl_12}[Co-authorship is also regulated by the Russian
Federation ]{.stl_10}[Civil Code]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[,]{.stl_10}^[163\ ]{.stl_16}^[which  establishes
that the persons who have jointly created a work are the
co-authors,  regardless of whether the work forms a single, inseparable
whole or consists of parts each  of which has independent significance.
A work created in co-authorship shall be jointly  used by co-authors,
unless otherwise agreed by them in writing. When such a work forms  an
inseparable whole, no co-author shall have the right to prohibit the use
of the work  without sufficient grounds for doing so. Part of a work
that can be independently used, ]{.stl_10}[ i.e., a part having
independent significance, may be used at the author's discretion unless
]{.stl_15}[ the co-authors have agreed otherwise in writing. Lastly,
each co-author shall have the  right to take measures to protect his or
her rights independently. The Russian Federation ]{.stl_10}[ Civil Code
]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[contains nothing definitive with
regard to the status of players involved in online  interactive gaming.
Neither statutory law nor judicial practice recognizes the
contributions  of online players as any sort of legal object.]{.stl_10}

[190. ]{.stl_12}[However, where the video game is considered a complex
object, the person or entity (i.e.,  a video game studio or producer)
that organizes the creation of such an object containing  several
protected results of intellectual activity shall obtain the right to use
these results  through a contract giving them exclusive rights or
through a license concluded with the  holders of the exclusive
rights]{.stl_10}^[164]{.stl_16}^[. ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[If the person who organizes the creation of
a complex  object obtains the right to use the result of intellectual
activity specially created, or to be  created, for inclusion in such a
complex object, the contract shall be considered to be a  transfer of
the exclusive right, unless otherwise agreed by the parties.]{.stl_10}

[191. ]{.stl_12}[The license to use a result of intellectual activity as
part of a complex object shall be  concluded for the whole time period
and with respect to the whole territory of the validity of  the
respective exclusive right, unless provided otherwise by the
contract.]{.stl_10}

[161 ]{.stl_07}[Article 1257 of the Russian Federation ]{.stl_09}[Civil
Code]{.stl_17 style="font-style:italic;"}[. ]{.stl_09}[162
]{.stl_07}[Article 1229 of the Russian Federation ]{.stl_09}[Civil
Code]{.stl_17 style="font-style:italic;"}[. ]{.stl_09}[163
]{.stl_07}[Article 1258 of the Russian Federation ]{.stl_09}[Civil
Code]{.stl_17 style="font-style:italic;"}[. ]{.stl_09}[164
]{.stl_07}[Article 1240 of the Russian Federation ]{.stl_09}[Civil

[page 65]{.stl_10}

[192. ]{.stl_12}[It is important to note that a licensing contract that
restricts the use of a result of  intellectual activity which forms part
of a complex object shall be considered invalid. In the  use of a
copyrighted work, the creator shall retain the right of authorship and
other  personal non-proprietary rights to such a result; however, the
person who organizes the  creation of the object shall have the right to
indicate his or her name or designation  thereon or to demand such an
indication.]{.stl_10}

[193. ]{.stl_12}[The Russian Federation has restrictive labor laws,
which means that issues relating to  employer-employee relationships
dominate in many markets, including interactive  entertainment. In that
regard, although an author may not only be considered an  employee, this
would generally be the case. ]{.stl_10}[This affects the author's legal
status as such ]{.stl_15}[ authors create video games as part of their
employment duties, but act in both employee  and author legal
capacities.]{.stl_10}

[TRANSFER OF RIGHTS]{.stl_10}

[194. ]{.stl_12}[The Russian Federation ]{.stl_10}[Civil Code]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[, Article 1295, provides that the copyright
in a work of ]{.stl_10}[ science, literature or art created within the
employee's (author's) labor obligations shall ]{.stl_15}[ belong to the
author. ]{.stl_10}[The exclusive right in an employee's work shall
belong to the ]{.stl_15}[ employer (e.g., a video game studio) unless a
labor contract or other contract between  the  employer and author
provides otherwise. If, within three years from the date on which
the  employee submits the work to the employer, that employer does not
begin to use the  work, transfer the exclusive right in it to another
person or inform the author that the work ]{.stl_10}[ is to be kept
secret; the exclusive right in the employee's work shall belong to the
author]{.stl_15}[.]{.stl_10}

[Additionally, if, within the term specified above, the employer begins
using the  ]{.stl_10}[employee's ]{.stl_15}[work or transfers the
exclusive right in it to another person, the author shall have the right
to demand remuneration. The author shall also have the right to demand
remuneration in ]{.stl_10}[cases where the employer decides to keep the
employee's work s]{.stl_15}[ecret and, for this reason, does not begin
to use the work within the above-mentioned term. The amount of
remuneration, and the conditions and procedure for its payment by the
employer, shall be defined in the employer-employee contract or, in case
of dispute, by a court.]{.stl_10}

[195. ]{.stl_12}[Where, according to the employment agreement, the
exclusive right in an employee's ]{.stl_15}[ work belongs to the author,
the employer shall have the right to use the work for purposes  related
to the employment task or within the limits deriving therefrom, as well
as to make  the work public unless otherwise provided for in the
employer-employee contract. In this ]{.stl_10}[ case, the right of the
author to use an employee's work for purposes not related to the
]{.stl_15}[ employment task, or for purposes related to the employment
task but beyond the limits  deriving therefrom, shall not be limited.
]{.stl_10}[Lastly, the employer may, in using an employee's
]{.stl_15}[ work, indicate his or her own name or designation or require
such an attribution.]{.stl_10}^[165]{.stl_16}^

[196. ]{.stl_12}[Should the video game be considered a computer program,
the provisions contained in  Article 1296 of the Russian Federation
]{.stl_10}[Civil Code ]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[should be
respected. This Article  establishes, among other things, that, where a
computer program or database  is created  under a contract, the subject
of which was its creation (on order), the exclusive right in  such a
computer program or database shall belong to the customer, unless
otherwise  provided by an agreement between the contractor (the
performer) and the customer. The  author of a computer program created
on order, to which the exclusive right in the]{.stl_10}

[165 ]{.stl_07}[Article 1295 of the Russian Federation ]{.stl_09}[Civil
Code]{.stl_17 style="font-style:italic;"}[.]{.stl_09}

[page 66]{.stl_10}

[program or database does not belong, shall have the right to demand
remuneration in]{.stl_10}

[accordance with the third subparagraph of paragraph 2, Article 1295, of
the ]{.stl_10}[Civil Code.]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}^[166]{.stl_16}^

[ECONOMIC COMPENSATION FOR AUTHORS]{.stl_10}

[197. ]{.stl_12}[Generally, in the video game industry, where companies
(video game studios) are  responsible for the development of a game,
compensation to authors is usually in the form  of salary. In the case
of independent contractors, the language of the agreement
prevails.  This usually involves a flat fee; however, other schemes,
such as royalty payments or a  combination of both, can exist.]{.stl_10}

[198. ]{.stl_12}[Therefore, video games are mainly protected as software
in the Russian Federation,  although experts consider them to be complex
works that can be protected through  different means. This complexity
means that the legal regime applicable for video games  is not clear,
especially in terms of the transfer of rights, authorship and
remuneration.]{.stl_10}

[RWANDA]{.stl_11}

[199. ]{.stl_12}[Law N° 31/2009 of October 26, 2009, the ]{.stl_10}[Law

]{.stl_10}[ and trademarks and ―]{.stl_15}[copyrights and related rights

[CLASSIFICATION]{.stl_10}

[201. ]{.stl_12}[The Rwandese ]{.stl_10}[Law on the Protection of
Intellectual Property ]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[makes no
specific mention  of the legal protection of not only video games, but
also audiovisual recordings. The video  game industry is undeveloped in
Rwanda and video games have yet to be given a legal  classification.
There is no law related to management of the industry and
the  jurisprudence or business practices are almost non-existent.
Therefore, one cannot talk  about a value chain or authors, producers,
publishers and, in general, stakeholders  regarding video games in
Rwanda.]{.stl_10}

[On a more theoretical level, any person that has created an original
work, in any form or shape, will be deemed the ]{.stl_10}[original owner
of moral and economic rights.]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}^[174\ ]{.stl_06
style="font-style:italic;"}^[Consequently, and as mentioned above, any
person that has created a work that, further on, has been incorporated
in a video game can be a contributor to the final work and, hence,
become a co-author of the work. In Rwanda there is no specific regime
for contributors to video games; therefore, the general rule shall apply
in this sense.]{.stl_10}

[CONTRIBUTORS]{.stl_10}

[202. ]{.stl_12}[Accordingly, video game authors can be freelance
contributors or employees of the  person or entity that is developing
this type of original work. In respect of a work created  by an author
employed by a natural person or legal entity in the course of
his/her  employment, the original owner of the moral and economic rights
may be, unless provided  otherwise in a contract, the employed author.
Nonetheless, the law is contradictory on  this point, because it states
that, in this case, the economic rights may be considered  assigned to
the employer or his/her representative to the extent necessary for
the  customary activities of the employer.]{.stl_10}^[175]{.stl_16}^

[Therefore, where a labor relationship exists, there is a presumption
that the employee \[second\] has transferred certain rights to the
employer for its customary activities, unless otherwise negotiated and
established in a contract. ]{.stl_10}[Finally, the law clarifies that
―]{.stl_15}[the rights that the author does not mention in the contract
are expressly reserved to him or ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[her.‖]{.stl_19
style="font-style:italic;"}^[176]{.stl_16}^

[In any case, the assignment contract shall be valid only if it is made
in writing and signed by the parties.]{.stl_10}^[177]{.stl_16}^

[203. ]{.stl_12}[The Rwandese ]{.stl_10}[Law on the Protection of
Intellectual Property ]{.stl_05 style="font-style:italic;"}[law is
silent on the different  kinds of financial compensation available to
authors, holding solely tha]{.stl_10}[t ―]{.stl_15}[the
assignment  contract shall contain the mode of remuneration for the
author in accordance with the use ]{.stl_05
style="font-style:italic;"}[ made to his work.‖]{.stl_19
style="font-style:italic;"}^[178]{.stl_16}^

[174 ]{.stl_07}[Article 222 of the Rwandese ]{.stl_09}[Law on the
